<title>Rock-Salt MnS0.5Se0.5 Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries | ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</title>

        <link rel="schema.DC" href="http://purl.org/DC/elements/1.0/"><meta name="citation_journal_title" content="ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces"><meta name="dc.Title" content="Rock-Salt MnS0.5Se0.5 Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta name="dc.Creator" content="Shiqi  Xing"><meta name="dc.Creator" content="Jing  Yang"><meta name="dc.Creator" content="Mairman  Muska"><meta name="dc.Creator" content="Huanran  Li"><meta name="dc.Creator" content="Qing  Yang"><meta name="dc.Subject" content="MnS0.5Se0.5 anode; MnS0.5Se0.5/N-doped graphene hybrid; interface-reinforced structure; van der Waals heterojunction; LIBs/SIBs; long-term stability"><meta name="dc.Description" content="Manganese-based chalcogenides would be of latent capacity in serving as anodes for assembling lithium- and/or sodium-ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs) due to their large theoretical capacity, low price, an..."><meta name="Description" content="Manganese-based chalcogenides would be of latent capacity in serving as anodes for assembling lithium- and/or sodium-ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs) due to their large theoretical capacity, low price, an..."><meta name="dc.Publisher" content="American Chemical Society"><meta name="dc.Date" scheme="WTN8601" content="May 10, 2021"><meta name="dc.Type" content="research-article"><meta name="dc.Format" content="text/HTML"><meta name="dc.Identifier" scheme="doi" content="10.1021/acsami.1c04776"><meta name="dc.Language" content="en"><meta name="dc.Coverage" content="world"><meta name="dc.Rights" content="© 2021 American Chemical Society"><meta name="keywords" content="MnS0.5Se0.5 anode,MnS0.5Se0.5/N-doped graphene hybrid,interface-reinforced structure,van der Waals heterojunction,LIBs/SIBs,long-term stability">

        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.1c04776"><meta property="og:title" content="Rock-Salt MnS0.5Se0.5 Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/acsami.1c04776.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Manganese-based chalcogenides would be of latent capacity in serving as anodes for assembling lithium- and/or sodium-ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs) due to their large theoretical capacity, low price, and low-toxicity functionality, while the low electroconductivity and easy agglomeration behavior may impede their technical applications. Here, a solid-state solution of MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes in rock-salt phase has been synthesized for the first time at a relatively low temperature from the precursors of Mn(II) acetylacetonate with dibenzyl dichalcogens in oleylamine with octadecene, and the MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes have been assembled with N-doped graphene to form a new kind of heterostructured nanohybrids (shortened as MnS0.5Se0.5/N-G hybrids), which are very potential for the fabrication of metal-ion batteries including LIBs and/or SIBs. Investigations revealed that there have been dense vacancies generated and active sites increased via nonequilibrium alloying of MnS and MnSe into the solid-solution MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes with segregation and defects achieved in the low-temperature solution synthetic route. Meanwhile, the introduction of N-doped graphene forming heterojunction interfaces between MnS0.5Se0.5 and N-doped graphene would efficiently enhance their electroconductivity and avoid agglomeration of the active MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes with considerably improved electrochemical properties. As a result, the MnS0.5Se0.5/N-G hybrids delivered superior Li/Na storage capacities with outstanding rate performance as well as satisfactorily lasting stability (1039/457 mA h g–1 at 0.1 A g–1 for LIBs/SIBs). Additionally, full-cell LIBs of the anodic MnS0.5Se0.5/N-G constructed with cathodic LiFePO4 (LFP) further confirmed the promising future for their practical application."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/acsami.1c04776.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6e3a1cfa1775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e3a1cfa1775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '9a19a346-8bb2-4552-9710-0862ba63b1a3'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e3a1cfa1775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="90f6e3a1cfa1775c-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rock-Salt MnS&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt;Se&lt;sub&gt;0.5&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c04776", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

China</div></div><div class="loa-info-scifinder"><span>More by <a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Mairman++Muska" data-id="article_author_search">Mairman Muska</a></span></div></div></div></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">Huanran Li</span><div class="loa-info hlFld-Affiliation"><div class="loa-info--wrapper"><div class="loa-info-name">Huanran Li</div><div class="loa-info-affiliations"><div class="loa-info-affiliations-info">Hefei National Laboratory of Physical Sciences at the Microscale (HFNL),&nbsp; Department of Chemistry &nbsp;and&nbsp; Laboratory of Nanomaterials for Energy Conversion (LNEC), University of Science and Technology of China (USTC), Hefei, Anhui 230026, P. Fax: +86-551-63606266.</span><span class="conrtib-corresp"></span><span class="conrtib-corresp"></span><span class="conrtib-corresp"></span><div class="loa-info-scifinder"><span>More by <a class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D22608%26pageCount%3D13%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DShiqi%2BXing%252C%2BJing%2BYang%252C%2BMairman%2BMuska%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D19%26contentID%3Dacsami.1c04776%26title%3DRock-Salt%2BMnS0.5Se0.5%2BNanocubes%2BAssembled%2Bon%2BN-Doped%2BGraphene%2BForming%2Bvan%2Bder%2BWaals%2BHeterostructured%2BHybrids%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BLithium-%2Band%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D13%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D22620%26publicationDate%3DMay%2B2021" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0010.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0010.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Manganese-based chalcogenides would be of latent capacity in serving as anodes for assembling lithium- and/or sodium-ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs) due to their large theoretical capacity, low price, and low-toxicity functionality, while the low electroconductivity and easy agglomeration behavior may impede their technical applications. Here, a solid-state solution of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes in rock-salt phase has been synthesized for the first time at a relatively low temperature from the precursors of Mn(II) acetylacetonate with dibenzyl dichalcogens in oleylamine with octadecene, and the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes have been assembled with N-doped graphene to form a new kind of heterostructured nanohybrids (shortened as MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids), which are very potential for the fabrication of metal-ion batteries including LIBs and/or SIBs. Investigations revealed that there have been dense vacancies generated and active sites increased via nonequilibrium alloying of MnS and MnSe into the solid-solution MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes with segregation and defects achieved in the low-temperature solution synthetic route. Meanwhile, the introduction of N-doped graphene forming heterojunction interfaces between MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> and N-doped graphene would efficiently enhance their electroconductivity and avoid agglomeration of the active MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes with considerably improved electrochemical properties. As a result, the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids delivered superior Li/Na storage capacities with outstanding rate performance as well as satisfactorily lasting stability (1039/457 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> for LIBs/SIBs). Additionally, full-cell LIBs of the anodic MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G constructed with cathodic LiFePO<sub>4</sub> (LFP) further confirmed the promising future for their practical application.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D22608%26pageCount%3D13%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DShiqi%2BXing%252C%2BJing%2BYang%252C%2BMairman%2BMuska%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D19%26contentID%3Dacsami.1c04776%26title%3DRock-Salt%2BMnS0.5Se0.5%2BNanocubes%2BAssembled%2Bon%2BN-Doped%2BGraphene%2BForming%2Bvan%2Bder%2BWaals%2BHeterostructured%2BHybrids%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BLithium-%2Band%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D13%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D22620%26publicationDate%3DMay%2B2021" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2021 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291980&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Nanocubes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Nanocubes" hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff"                         of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Mns0.5se0.5+Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_MnS0.5Se0.5%20anode">MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> anode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Mns0.5se0.5%2Fn-doped+Graphene+Hybrid&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_MnS0.5Se0.5%2FN-doped%20graphene%20hybrid">MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-doped graphene hybrid</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Interface-reinforced+Structure&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_interface-reinforced%20structure">interface-reinforced structure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Van+Der+Waals+Heterojunction&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_van%20der%20Waals%20heterojunction">van der Waals heterojunction</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Libs%2Fsibs&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_LIBs%2FSIBs">LIBs/SIBs</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Long-term+Stability&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_long-term%20stability">long-term stability</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">In modern society, developing efficient energy storage systems (ESS) with high efficiency and low price is of high importance to meet the ever-growing scale of the energy market. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> Among all ESS strategies, rechargeable secondary batteries (RSBs) have been proven to be a successful way that can be applied almost everywhere even from little toys to giant spaceships. In particular, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) hold tremendous promise due to their virtues of low price, environment friendliness, portability, and high power density. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2 ref3 ref4'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 2 to 4">(2−4)</a> Recently, LIBs have intensively been demonstrated as a successful ESS, especially for applications in portable devices and newly emerged electric vehicles (EVs). Meanwhile, due to the same storage mechanism as LIBs and abundant availability, SIBs are considered to be a cheaper substitute for LIBs. As a result, there have been extensive efforts made to develop electrode materials for LIBs and SIBs with improved performance.</div><div class="NLM_p">Currently, the anode of Li/Na-ion batteries has been reported considerably over carbon-based materials, metallic compounds (mainly including oxides/complex oxides, sulfides, selenides, phosphides, etc.), Si/Si-based, alloy-based materials, and organic materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 5 to 15">(5−15)</a> Among them, transition-metal chalcogenides (TMCs) have been intensively designed and explored in terms of their easily manipulated synthetic procedure and fabrication, relatively low price, and excellent performance in both Li and Na storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16 ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 16 and 17">(16,17)</a> As a typical member of TMCs, manganese-based chalcogenides received increasing interest as LIB/SIB anode materials due to their nontoxicity, great abundance, and low-voltage plateau. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21" aria-label="reference 18 to 21">(18−21)</a> In detail, Hao et al. reported α-MnS composites for LIBs with a capacity of 232.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> over 600 cycles at a current density of 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> Li et al. reported nanostructured α-MnSe for LIBs with a capacity of 150 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 5000 cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> Xu et al. fabricated MnS/RGO nanosheets with capacities of ∼830/∼308 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> for LIBs/SIBs, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> Also, α-MnSe@N-doped carbon composites were fabricated by Liu et al. and were intensively investigated for application of both LIBs (∼800 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>) and SIBs (∼400 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> However, it is no doubt that there are still some apparent drawbacks in the transition-metal compounds, including manganese-based chalcogenides. Their electrochemical properties should be improved largely to meet the requirements for technical applications, although they are very potential to work as anodes. In typical, there are two fundamental issues to be concerned and explored to enhance and improve the performance of manganese-based chalcogenides serving as anode materials. The first barrier is the intrinsically low electrical conductivity of the manganese-based chalcogenides, which limits the output practically with a high capacity. To solve this problem, introducing various kinds of carbon materials was proven to be an efficient method to enhance the electrical conductivity and support the structure as the framework. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11 ref12 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27" aria-label="reference 11, 12 and 20 to 27">(11,12,20−27)</a> On the other hand, the second problem is how to expose more active sites while reducing diffusion pathways for Li/Na ions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> As noted, the active electrode materials could be largely expanded in surface area when they are fabricated with reduced size, especially compared to the bulk material. Also, nanocrystals with smaller sizes would be capable of presenting some more active sites comparably. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> However, it cannot be ignored that even if the active materials are nanocrystallized in small size, a problem still remained since according to thermodynamics, possible agglomeration cannot be easily prevented in the system, which will waste and even deplete the effort of such nanocrystallization. Therefore, there would be a balance between the aspects to reduce the active electrode materials with smaller size and to avoid the agglomeration effectively, while in general, it is still a challenge to tune an optimal size for the electrodes although there has been so much progress achieved to date.</div><div class="NLM_p">As reported, vacancy engineering has been applied as an alternative strategy to generate active sites for electrode materials. The vacancies can generate more active sites by remodeling the electronic structure and redistribution of electrons, which can absorb more Li/Na ions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30 ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 30 and 31">(30,31)</a> For example, by alloying MoS<sub>2</sub> and MoSe<sub>2</sub>, anion vacancies can be generated <i>in situ</i> in the nanocrystals. When a 1:1 molar ratio of S and Se is selected, there is the largest vacancy concentration generated in MoSSe compared to different ratios between MoS<sub>2</sub> and MoSe<sub>2</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> Similar strategies have also been demonstrated in M<i><sub>x</sub></i>SSe (M = metals like Sn, Cr, etc.) <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33 ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33 ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 33 to 35">(33−35)</a> that would be promising and technically potential in the future as an electrode for alkali-ion batteries.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In view of this point <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22 ref23 ref33 ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22 ref23 ref33 ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 22, 23 and 33 to 35">(22,23,33−35)</a> along with our recent investigations, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref36" aria-label="reference 28 and 36">(28,36)</a> we promoted a moderate and straightforward one-pot solution-phase route to the nonequilibrium alloyed solid-state solution MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes first at a relatively low temperature and assembled them with N-doped graphene (N-G) heterostructurally aiming to fabricate a kind of enhanced hybrids with dense structure and property-modulated interfaces for Li/Na-ion storage. Such designed hybrids would be able to solve the as-mentioned problems with improved electrochemical performances based on the following aspects: (1) alloyed nanostructures with densely stabilized and exposed active components achieved under nonequilibrium conditions at relatively low temperatures; (2) anchored active components on N-G preventing possible agglomeration but generating dense functional interfaces over the hybridization; (3) enhanced electroconductivity and strengthened mechanical property efficiently through interface structure regulation at heterojunction areas; and (4) generated dense vacancies and active sites over segregations/defects within the alloyed nanostructures besides the heterostructured interfaces favorable for Li/Na-ion storage. It turned out the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids showed prominent capacities of ∼1039 and ∼457 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> (for LIBs and SIBs, respectively, over 80/100 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>), desirable rate performance, and excellent long-term stability. Moreover, the full cells for LIBs of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G//LiFePO<sub>4</sub> have been constructed that are capable of supplying 37 red light light-emitting diode (LED) bulbs at the same time with a single cell, which confirmed that the as-fabricated MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids are promising for potential technical applications, especially in energy storage systems.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Synthesis of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> Nanocubes</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The synthesis of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes was carried out through a simple one-pot route via the reaction of Mn(II) acetylacetonate with dibenzyl dichalcogens in a mixed media of oleylamine and octadecene. Representatively, 0.2 mmol of manganese acetylacetonate (50.63 mg), 0.05 mmol of dibenzyl disulfide (12.32 mg), and 0.05 mmol of dibenzyl diselenide (17.01 mg) were introduced into a 100 mL three-neck flask together with ligand and solvent of oleylamine (4 mL) and 1-octadecene (2 mL). To remove moisture and possible impurities, the reaction temperatures were first elevated to 150 °C and kept for 30 min under argon flow besides magnetic stirring. After that, the mixed solution was raised to 320 °C lasting 10 min before it was cooled down naturally. Subsequently, the centrifuged MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes with a thorough washing of toluene and isopropanol were collected for the assembly with N-doped graphene (N-G) to form MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids for further studies.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Synthesis of N-G</h3><div class="NLM_p last">First, graphene oxide was synthesized from graphite powder through the Hummers’ method. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> Then, N-G was synthesized following our previous work. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> In brief, 10 mg of graphene oxide and 400 mg of urea were dissolved in 25 mL of water under intensive ultrasonication. After ultrasonicated for 30 min, the homogeneous mixture was reacted in an autoclave at 160 °C for 3 h. Finally, the black sample was collected by centrifugation, washed with deionized water several times, and dried for further use. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a></div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Fabrication of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G Hybrids</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids were fabricated through a self-assembly strategy in the solution-phase processing. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> Briefly, the as-synthesized MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes were dispersed in toluene and further mixed with another toluene solution containing different amounts of N-G. The mixture solution of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> with N-G was sonicated for 1 h to a kind of heterostructured hybrids. Finally, the hybrid composites were vacuum-dried and heated in Ar/H<sub>2</sub>(3% H<sub>2</sub>) flow at 250 °C for 2 h to ensure they are assembled to be a stable heterojunction-like structure.</div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7">2.4.  Structure Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The crystalline phase and phase purity were checked by a Rigaku TTR-III X-ray diffractometer (incident source: Cu Kα<sub>1</sub> radiation, λ = 1.54182 Å). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> Morphological analyses were performed by electron microscopy techniques, including scanning electron microscopy (SEM) (JEOL JSM-6700F) and normal transmission electron microscopy (TEM) (Hitachi H-7700). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> High-resolution TEM (HRTEM), selected area electron diffraction (SAED), high-angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM), and affiliated energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX) mapping analyses were executed on a JEOL JEM-ARF200F TEM/STEM supplied with a spherical aberration corrector. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> The valence states of the elements were checked by X-ray photoelectron spectra (XPS) using a PerkinElmer ESCALAB 250 spectrometer. The products were also characterized via Raman spectroscopy with an excitation source of 532 nm over Lab-RAM HR UV/VIS/NIR. At the same time, the Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) method was applied to measure the specific surface areas of both isolated MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes and MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids using a Micromeritic TriStar II 3020 V1.03 instrument (Micromeritics Instrument Corporation). Meanwhile, the carbon content of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids was analyzed by thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) using an SDT Q600 TG-DTA analyzer in air.</div></div><div id="sec2_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8">2.5.  Electrochemical Test</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Half-cell coin-type batteries (CR-2016 type) were constructed in an argon atmosphere glovebox to evaluate the performance of LIBs/SIBs for MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids compared with MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>. In detail, a slurry was made by mixing the products of pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes or MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids with Ketjen Black and poly(vinylidene difluoride) in an 80:10:10 ratio by weight applying N-methyl pyrrolidone as the solvent. Such slurry mixtures were hand-milled over 2 h and then smeared on cleaned copper foil with uniform thickness. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref36" aria-label="reference 28 and 36">(28,36)</a> The copper foil was then treated in vacuum at 80 °C for 12 h. After complete drying, it was cut into round pieces. The active material mass loadings were set as ca. 1.2–1.5 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. In the assembly of half-cell LIBs, the cathodes were performed using MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids, the anodes were lithium foil, and the separators were Celgard 2400 pieces. The electrolyte for LIBs was the solution of 1.0 M LiPF<sub>6</sub> in ethylene carbonate (EC)/diethyl carbonate (DEC) = 1:1 vol % with 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC). Similarly, in the half-cell SIBs, the cathodes were MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids, the anodes were sodium foil, the separators were Whatman GF/F glass fiber. The electrolyte for SIBs was the solution of 1.0 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in 100% diglyme. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> For full-cell LIBs, commercial LFP was employed as the cathode, with MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrodes as the anode. The mass loading for LFP is about 6 times larger than that for the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid anode. Both LFP cathode and MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid anode were activated for three cycles with lithium metal counter electrode at low current densities before assembling the full batteries. The galvanostatic charge/discharge curves were obtained from a LAND-CT2001A. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) tests at different sweep rates and the electrochemistry impedance spectroscopy (EIS) were conducted in a CHI 760E electrochemical workstation.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The synthetic procedure to monodisperse MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes and the subsequent self-assembly of the nanocubes on N-G to form the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids is schematically illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a besides the description in the <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sec2" aria-label="Experimental Section">Experimental Section</a>. The hybrids were integrated by van der Waals force, forming van der Waals-type heterostructured composites, which would provide sufficient stability against electrochemical reactions under severe conditions on the basis of investigations on Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>- and FePSe<sub>3</sub>-based systems. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref36" aria-label="reference 28 and 36">(28,36)</a></div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0002.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Schematic synthesis route to MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids, (b) X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes, N-G, and MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids, and (c) scheme of crystal structure for active MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">XRD patterns for MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes, N-G, and their binary hybrids are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b. The detected pattern of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes in the six-coordinate bonding rock-salt phase (black) matched perfectly with the standard card JCPDS no. 01-089-4955 (lattice constants: <i>a</i> = 5.346 Å, α = 90°). In detail, the peaks at 33.5, 48.1, 59.9, and 70.4° (2θ) can be assigned to the (200), (220), (222), and (400) facets of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>, respectively, when both S and Se atoms occupy in disorder. However, there could be an asymmetric feature of diffraction peaks detected in the magnified pattern (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>), revealing a detectable decrease in crystallinity. The decrease in crystallinity often results from the possible generation of segregations in the disordered solid-state solutions including the present MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes grown at relatively low temperatures, which is similar to the ones in PbSe<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<sub>1–<i>x</i></sub> nanocrystals via nonequilibrium growth, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a> especially along with point defects, relevant to distortion and disorder within MoSSe, MoS<sub>2(1–<i>x</i>)</sub>Se<sub>2<i>x</i></sub>, and CdTe/CdS. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref39 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 32, 39 and 40">(32,39,40)</a> The XRD pattern in blue color shows the result obtained for N-doped graphene with the (002) diffraction peak. As for the hybrid sample, the XRD pattern (in orange) reveals the presence of diffraction peaks for both nanocubes and N-doped graphene, which proves that the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes successfully anchored onto N-G.</div><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c is the schematic structure of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes, displaying a typical NaCl-type structure with the <i>Fm</i>3̅<i>m</i> space group in a disordered form of solid-state solution between the endmembers of MnS and MnSe. In detail, manganese ions occupy the positions of sodium ions while sulfur or selenium ions randomly take the place of chloride ions. Raman spectroscopy was also checked to verify the chemical composition and structure. From <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>, three peaks can be clearly found in Raman spectra. The first peak lying in the Raman shift region of 580–700 cm<sup>–1</sup> comes from the intrinsic vibration mode of Mn–S and Mn–Se, which is supported by XRD results. The imitated peaks are shown in detail in the inset of <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>, with the peaks of Mn–S and Mn–Se located at about 628 and 655 cm<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, which are well indexed to the previous report on α-MnS and α-MnSe. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41 ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref42" aria-label="reference 41 and 42">(41,42)</a> The other two peaks centered at high wavenumbers of ∼1353 and ∼1586 cm<sup>–1</sup> show typical features of disordered carbon and graphitic carbon that are known as D and G bands. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> It is deduced that the peak intensity ratio between D and G bands is 0.94 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>), suggesting that the N-doped graphene is of higher graphitization.</div><div class="NLM_p">To identify the morphological features, both pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes and MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids were illustrated using TEM and SEM. From TEM images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a,b, in different magnifications), the pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocrystals showed excellent monodispersity with a uniform cubic shape, followed by the cubic symmetric crystal structure. The sizes of the majority isolated nanocubes were counted in the range of 19–24 nm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b, inset). After a solution-phase self-assembly process (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d,e, in different magnifications), the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes were successfully anchored on the N-G surface through van der Waals force and formed a kind of heterojunction-like hybrids. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> All of the nanocubes were uniformly distributed onto the surface of N-doped graphene without any individual particle outside detected. As a comparison, the pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes aggregated to a larger cluster after they were dried, as shown in the SEM images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c). Through introducing N-G to the system forming the hybrids, the component of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes distributed evenly with good monodispersity onto N-G (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>f), generating dense functional interfaces in between MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> and N-G probably with strengthened structures and enhanced functionalities.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0003.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. TEM images in different magnifications and SEM images of pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes (a–c) and MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids (d–f). The inset in (b) shows the size distribution of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">From their BET results (as seen in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>), the surface areas of the agglomerated bare MnS<sub>05</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes and the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids were determined to be 12.19 and 45.72 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. The surface area is nearly 3 times larger than that of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes after they were assembled on N-G. The large surface area is mainly contributed by the sheetlike geometry of N-G, and the division of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes on N-G prevented agglomeration. There are more active sites generated with the increase of the specific surface areas in the hybrids, and the electrolyte can fully get in contact with the active electrode materials, based on the recent investigations of a ternary system (Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/g-C<sub>3</sub>N<sub>4</sub>/N-G). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">To further reveal the microstructures of the monodisperse MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes, we also performed HRTEM determinations at the same time. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a, there are two lattices detected with distances of 0.267 and 0.187 nm, which match the ideal distance of (200) and (220) planes, respectively, for MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes. As measured, the angle between the two detected planes is 45°, which is in accordance with the theoretical angle between the two facets. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b, there are fast Fourier transform (FFT) pattern, HAADF-STEM image, and EDX mappings detected for the pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes. The FFT image shows two sets of diffraction spots representing (200) and (220) facets, consistent with the XRD result (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b) and confirming the purity of single-crystalline MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes in the cubic rock-salt phase. The EDX elemental mappings (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b) show that the Mn element was evenly distributed within the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes while S and Se elements were not so homogeneous as Mn was. Also, as seen from the STEM-EDX line scan (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c), the signals of the three elements remained stable with the intensities of S and Se roughly equal to each other. However, in the segregation region, the amounts of S and Se would be a little different. Meanwhile, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>, the EDX spectrum revealed that the overall atomic ratios of Mn, S, and Se elements are 49.2, 25.7, and 25.1%, respectively, close to the ideal atomic ratio (2:1:1). Although the overall atomic ratio fits the theoretical ratio, the alloying is still uneven in the partial area. As can be witnessed in the HAADF-STEM image of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b, some partial areas with lower contrast suggest that there are segregations remained in the nanocubes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a> This uneven alloying had been reported to be a common phenomenon in the solid-state solution of metal sulfides and selenides due to a fast growth at relatively low temperatures, which is related to the generation of distortions and vacancies, thus improving the electrochemical performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref44 ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref44 ref45" aria-label="reference 32, 44 and 45">(32,44,45)</a> The nanoscale dislocations can be further confirmed from the magnified HAADF-STEM image (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>). The SAED pattern of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d) showed three diffraction rings, which can be assigned to the (200), (220), and (222) planes of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> with a very faint diffraction ring, which is the (002) plane of N-doped graphene. Similarly, from the HAADF-STEM and EDX mappings of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d), the homogeneous distribution of Mn, S, and Se from MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> together with C and N from N-doped graphene was confirmed, suggesting the successful construction of the binary-component hybrids. Furthermore, as witnessed by the HRTEM determination (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>), there are clear lattice overlaps between MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> and N-doped graphene, which further prove the existence of heterointerface in the hybrids.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0004.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) HRTEM images of pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes; (b) FFT pattern, HAADF-STEM images, and EDX mappings of pure MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes; (c) STEM-EDX line scan for a single MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocube; and (d) SAED pattern, HAADF-STEM images, and EDX mappings of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">XPS analysis was also employed to detect the chemical composition of these MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids in the present work. From the result of the XPS survey spectrum (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>f), elements including Mn, S, Se, C, N, and O (coming from surface oxidation) were detected, which matches well with the results of EDX mapping analysis. The detailed XPS spectra for Mn 2p, S 2p, Se 3d, C 1s, and N 1s are illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a–e, respectively. The peaks located at 642.3 and 653.6 eV can be indexed to Mn 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and 2p<sub>1/2</sub> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a), respectively, which agree with previous studies. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19 ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19 ref41" aria-label="reference 19 and 41">(19,41)</a> The satellite peaks of Mn 2p at 641.0 and 645.7 eV may arise from the multiple splitting of energy levels, which are the evidence of intensive interaction between Mn and carbon. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46" aria-label="reference 46">(46)</a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b shows the peaks of S 2p and Se 3d. In detail, peaks of S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and 2p<sub>1/2</sub> are located at 162.1 and 163.7 eV, while peaks of Se 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and 2p<sub>1/2</sub> are located at 161.1 and 166.9 eV, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39 ref47'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39 ref47" aria-label="reference 39 and 47">(39,47)</a> The peak centered at 165.1 eV represents the connection of S and C, while the peaks at 168.5 eV were caused by surface oxidation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46 ref48 ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46 ref48 ref49" aria-label="reference 46, 48 and 49">(46,48,49)</a> The Se 3d spectrum (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c) exhibits three peaks with binding energies located at 55.4, 56.3, and 58.7 eV, which can be indexed to the peaks of Se 3d<sub>5/2</sub>, 3d<sub>3/2</sub>, and Se–O/Se–C, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42 ref50'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42 ref50" aria-label="reference 42 and 50">(42,50)</a> The high-resolution XPS spectrum of C 1s (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>d) shows five peaks at 284.8, 285.9, 286.9, 287.5, and 288.8 eV, which can be assigned to C–C, C–N, C–O/C–Mn, C═O, and O–C═O, respectively, in good agreement with previous reports. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref42 ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref42 ref46" aria-label="reference 28, 42 and 46">(28,42,46)</a> The peaks centered at the binding energies of 398.6, 400.0, 402.0, and 405.8 eV correspond to N 1s (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>e) of pyridinic-N, pyrrolic-N, graphitic-N, and oxidized-N. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref28" aria-label="reference 21 and 28">(21,28)</a> All of the elements show the typical peaks of connection between MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes and C, which are the evidence of the successful construction of the van der Waals heterojunction between the nanocubes and N-G through the self-assembly process. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref51 ref52 ref53 ref54'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref51 ref52 ref53 ref54" aria-label="reference 28 and 51 to 54">(28,51−54)</a> The C–Mn/C–S/C–Se bonds at the interface of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G heterojunction would reduce the electron gathering polarization, which leads to a faster electron transfer. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a></div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0005.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a–e) XPS spectra of Mn 2p, S 2p, Se 3d, C 1s, and N 1s, respectively, and (f) survey spectrum of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical behaviors over MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids as anodes for LIBs had been carried out to reveal the corresponding lithium storage potentials. The CR-2016 half-cell batteries were constructed using MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrodes (see the <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sec2" aria-label="Experimental Section">Experimental Section</a> for detailed information). All of the tests were performed in a voltage window of 0.01–3.00 V versus Li<sup>+</sup>/Li. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a shows the CV curves for the initial three cycles at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. There are three reduction peaks detected in the first cathodic scan.
