The first broad peak from 1.3 to 1.7 V can be assigned to the insertion of Li<sup>+</sup> into MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> to form Li<i><sub>x</sub></i>MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> based on the investigations of the MnS system. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref48" aria-label="reference 18 and 48">(18,48)</a> The second peak located at ∼0.53 V is relevant to the formation of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) and a phase change from α-MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> to β-MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>, which has already been reported on similar materials such as MnSe. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41 ref42 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref42 ref48" aria-label="reference 41, 42 and 48">(41,42,48)</a> The third peak emerged at ∼0.13 V was reported to be responsible for the formation of metallic Mn together with the final products Li<sub>2</sub>S and Li<sub>2</sub>Se. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55 ref56'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref55 ref56" aria-label="reference 55 and 56">(55,56)</a></div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0006.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Lithium storage performance of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrodes in half-cell battery system: (a) CV curves, (b) charge/discharge profiles, (c) comparison of cycling performances over both isolated MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes and hybrids at a current density of 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, (d) rate performance, and (e) long-term stability test.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">After the first cathodic scan, it shows a good overlap for the rest of CV scans, suggesting good stability of the subsequent charge/discharge process. In the following anodic scan, the peak at ∼1.35 V is attributed to the oxidation of metallic Mn to Mn<sup>2+</sup>, whereas the peaks at ∼1.90 and ∼2.54 V correspond to the stepwise deintercalation of Li<sup>+</sup> from Li<i><sub>x</sub></i>MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> over the determinations of MnS and MnSe. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref41 ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref41 ref42" aria-label="reference 18, 41 and 42">(18,41,42)</a> In the second cathodic scan, a new peak at ∼0.27 V appears, which is corresponds to the generation of metallic Mn, Li<sub>2</sub>S, and Li<sub>2</sub>Se. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48 ref57'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48 ref57" aria-label="reference 48 and 57">(48,57)</a> The peak position shift is mainly due to the phase change and the subsequent structural transformation of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> material, based on the previous investigation of MnSe. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref55" aria-label="reference 55">(55)</a> To further support the mechanism proposed by CV, we performed <i>ex situ</i> XRD tests for LIBs (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>) at the same time. In the XRD patterns, besides the diffraction peaks of Cu from the copper current collector, there are still two peaks of (200) and (220) planes for α-MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> clearly detected in the fresh batteries. When they were discharged to 2.0 and 1.0 V, the diffraction peaks of (200) and (220) planes shifted to a lower 2θ degree with expanded lattices, indicating the insert of Li<sup>+</sup> into MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> forming Li<i><sub>x</sub></i>MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>. When they were discharged to 0.01 V, the diffraction peaks of α-MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> disappeared, while the ones of Li<sub>2</sub>S and Li<sub>2</sub>Se were recorded. In the first charge process, the diffraction peaks of Li<sub>2</sub>S and Li<sub>2</sub>Se gradually disappeared, whereas the peaks of β-MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> appeared instead. Based on the CV tests and <i>ex situ</i> XRD determinations, the mechanism of Li<sup>+</sup> storage can be described as follows<disp-formula-group><figcaption><strong></strong><span class="figure__caption hlFld-FigureCaption"><p>First lithiation:</p></span></figcaption><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i10"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div></span></disp-formula-group><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m002.gif" alt="" id="_i11"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div></span><disp-formula-group><figcaption><strong></strong><span class="figure__caption hlFld-FigureCaption"><p>In the subsequent cycles:</p></span></figcaption><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq3"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m003.gif" alt="" id="_i12"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(3)</span></div></div></span></disp-formula-group>The charge/discharge curves for the initial three cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> are presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>b, which reveals that the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrode delivered initial lithiation and delithiation of ∼1508 and ∼856 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, upon which the Coulombic efficiency (CE) for the first cycle is calculated to be 56.8%. During the first cycle, the low CE probably resulted from an irreversible phase conversion from α-MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> to β-MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> and SEI film formation together with the decomposition of electrolyte. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19 ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19 ref42" aria-label="reference 18, 19 and 42">(18,19,42)</a> The lithium storage performance of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrode is displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c–e, where the charge and discharge processes of the anode in half-cells correspond to the discharge and charge ones in the full cells, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58 ref59'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref58 ref59" aria-label="reference 58 and 59">(58,59)</a> As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c, under the current density of 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, the discharge/charge specific capacity (similarly hereinafter) of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrode increased steadily with an activation process to ∼1039/1026 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> over 80 cycles and a high average Coulombic efficiency over 99%, suggesting superior reversibility. This activation process is a common phenomenon in many carbon-coated materials, mainly due to the generated structural defects on carbon material and the “pocket effect” for the hybrids. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref60 ref61 ref62 ref63'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref60 ref61 ref62 ref63" aria-label="reference 28 and 60 to 63">(28,60−63)</a> In comparison, at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> electrodes without integration of N-G can only deliver a capacity of ∼827/427 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with a Coulombic efficiency of 51.6% in the initial cycle and ∼253/250 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> over 80 trails. The Coulombic efficiencies of bare MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> are also inferior to those assembled on N-G, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c (top).</div><div class="NLM_p">Furthermore, the rate performances (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>d) of these two electrodes were examined under variable current densities of 100, 200, 500, 1000, 2000, 5000, 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, and finally drop back to 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, which lasted 10 cycles for each density. The MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrodes delivered reversible capacities of 901, 846, 810, 767, 738, 706, 841, and 1065 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, indicating satisfactory rate performance. By contrast, the bare MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> electrodes can only deliver capacities of 538, 442, 223, 129, 79, 41, 130, and 557 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, which showed colossal capacity degradation under high current densities. The poor capacity may be on account of the severe agglomeration of the bare materials, which greatly hindered the contact of Li<sup>+</sup> with inner material, which made the insertion difficult. In the long-term stability test (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>e), the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrodes maintained a specific capacity of ∼563/561 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 1000 trials, with a capacity retention of 84.4% (compared with the first reversible discharge capacity), revealing perfect long-term stability. The hybrid electrodes showed superior behavior to the bare electrodes, which is mainly due to the formation of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G heterointerface and thus enhanced the electroconductivity of the electrode. Thereafter, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was measured for fresh batteries of these two materials from 100 to 0.1 Hz. From the Nyquist plots (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>), a much smaller semicircle for MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrode can be seen. The charge transfer resistances (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) for bare and hybrid electrodes are measured to be 604 and 86 Ω, reflecting that assembling MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> on N-G can effectively reduce the resistance due to the enhancement of N-G-introduced interfaces. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref64 ref65 ref66'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref64 ref65 ref66" aria-label="reference 28 and 64 to 66">(28,64−66)</a> Furthermore, the 2D plane of N-G can effectively support MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes and limit their possible agglomeration due to the connected heterojunction-like interfaces that will also expose some more active sites based on the specific surface area determination (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>). The TEM images of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrode after 300 charge/discharge trails are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>, which reveals that the N-G can still support the active material efficiently over the repeated electrochemical intercalation/deintercalation.</div><div class="NLM_p">The SIB performances of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids were also studied using a half-cell system in 0.01–3.00 V. The CV curves for the initial three cycles are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a. Three peaks emerged at ∼1.63, ∼0.68, and ∼0.13 V, respectively, in the first cathodic scan. The reduction peaks at ∼1.63 and ∼0.13 V probably correspond to the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> into MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> and the generation of metallic Mn together with Na-S/Se compounds, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46 ref67'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46 ref67" aria-label="reference 46 and 67">(46,67)</a> while the broad peak at ∼0.68 V may attribute to the SEI layer generation and possible phase transition. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21 ref41 ref46 ref67'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref41 ref46 ref67" aria-label="reference 21, 41, 46 and 67">(21,41,46,67)</a> In the subsequent anodic scan, the oxidation peaks at ∼0.81, ∼1.52, ∼2.03, and ∼2.19 V are associated with the multistep conversion from metallic Mn to MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>, which is very close to the investigations of α-MnS and α-MnSe in the SIB system. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41 ref46 ref57 ref67'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref46 ref57 ref67" aria-label="reference 41, 46, 57 and 67">(41,46,57,67)</a> From the second cycle onward, the shifted reduction peak of ∼0.13 to ∼0.25 V is also attributed to the SEI formation and structural change, which is similar to the CV curves of LIB tests. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46 ref67'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46 ref67" aria-label="reference 46 and 67">(46,67)</a> Due to the similarity of mechanism between LIBs and SIBs, the reaction equation can be described as follows<disp-formula-group><figcaption><strong></strong><span class="figure__caption hlFld-FigureCaption"><p>First sodiation:</p></span></figcaption><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m004.gif" alt="" id="_i13"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div></span></disp-formula-group><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq5"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m005.gif" alt="" id="_i14"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(5)</span></div></div></span><disp-formula-group><figcaption><strong></strong><span class="figure__caption hlFld-FigureCaption"><p>In the subsequent cycles:</p></span></figcaption><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq6"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m006.gif" alt="" id="_i15"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(6)</span></div></div></span></disp-formula-group>The charge/discharge curves for SIB at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> are displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b, matching well with the peaks in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a. The first charge and discharge capacities are determined to be 420.6 and 618.6 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively (initial Coulombic efficiency: 68.0%). Likewise, a similar activation process occurred. The specific capacity slightly increased to 457/458 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 continuous trails (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>c). Meanwhile, the bare MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> electrodes delivered the first capacity of 549/259 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, and after 100 cycles, only 184/184 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> remained. The rate performance of SIBs was further evaluated (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>d). The current densities changed from 100 to 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup> gradually and finally dropped back to 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. The reversible capacities of hybrid electrodes are 395, 385, 352, 319, 293, and 447 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>. In contrast, the unsatisfactory capacities of 286, 251, 159, 115, 90, and 238 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> are delivered by the bare electrode. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>e is the long-term SIB test for the hybrid electrode, which shows that after 400 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the specific capacity still remained to be 340/339 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> that is still slightly larger than that of the second discharge due to the activation process (capacity retention: 101%, compared with the first reversible discharge capacity).</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0007.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Sodium storage performance of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrodes in half-cell battery system: (a) CV curves, (b) comparison of charge/discharge profiles with isolated MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes, (c) cycling performance, (d) rate performance, and (e) long-term stability.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To understand the effect of the N-doped graphene in the composite material, we constructed MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids with different loaded N-G ratios (termed as MSS/NG-1, 2, and 3, of which MSS/NG-1 has been performed as seen in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a> and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>), and the corresponding carbon ratios were identified by TGA measurements. As illustrated in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10f</a>, it is revealed the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids changed to Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> finally after TGA tests in the air atmosphere. The carbon ratios for MSS/NG-1, 2, and 3 were determined as 52.6, 40.4, and 26.8 wt %, respectively. Meanwhile, the cycling performances of MSS/NG-1, 2, and 3 were tested. As observed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10d,e</a>, MSS/NG-1 with the highest carbon ratio delivered the best performance in both capacity and stability, which further proves the importance of N-G involved in the hybrids. The above result reveals that the participation of N-doped graphene in the bare isolated MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes not only avoided the agglomeration but also enhanced the conductivity of the bare nanocubes. All of these roles mentioned above as well as their own participation in the metal-ion storage ensured the potential of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids for fabricating both Li/Na-ion batteries as an ideal anode, which is consistent with varied electrode materials integrated with graphene and/or carbon-based systems. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref12 ref28 ref36 ref68 ref69 ref70 ref71 ref72'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref12 ref28 ref36 ref68 ref69 ref70 ref71 ref72" aria-label="reference 5, 12, 28, 36 and 68 to 72">(5,12,28,36,68−72)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">To further study the electrochemical kinetics of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids for LIBs, CV measurements at incremental scanning speeds (0.1–1.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>) were tested (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a). The peak current (<i>i</i>) and the sweep rates obey the following equation and its variation expression <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref48 ref73'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref48 ref73" aria-label="reference 28, 48 and 73">(28,48,73)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq7"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m007.gif" alt="" id="_i16"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(7)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq8"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m008.gif" alt="" id="_i17"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(8)</span></div></div></span>There are two constants in the equation, <i>a</i> and <i>b</i>, which can be calculated by linear fitting for the plots of ln(sweep rate) versus ln(peak current). The slopes for the fitted lines are the values of <i>b</i>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref48" aria-label="reference 28 and 48">(28,48)</a> When it approaches 0.5, the Li/Na-ion storage reaction is mainly controlled by ion diffusion, whereas its value close to 1 suggests that the capacitive behavior is predominant. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref48" aria-label="reference 28 and 48">(28,48)</a> In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>b, the <i>b</i> values of six peaks marked in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a are fitted to be 0.918, 0.709, 0.993, 0.866, 0.951, and 0.846, respectively, indicating that capacitive reactions mainly control these peaks except for peak 2.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0008.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0008.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. Kinetic analysis of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids for half-cell LIBs: (a) CV curves at various sweep rates, (b) plots of ln(sweep rate) versus ln(peak current) and the fitted lines with b value, (c) CV curve at 0.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup> and the fitted capacitive contribution, and (d) capacitive contribution ratios.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Moreover, the ratio of capacitive and ion-diffusion reaction contributions follows the formula <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref73'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref73" aria-label="reference 73">(73)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq9"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_m009.gif" alt="" id="_i18"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(9)</span></div></div></span>where <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> represent capacitive and ion-diffusion contributions for <i>i</i> (the CV current), respectively, and <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub> are two constants. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref73'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref73" aria-label="reference 73">(73)</a> The currents (<i>i</i>) under different sweep rates (<i>v</i>) can be read from <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a, and the corresponding polynomial fittings for the above equation were carried out to determine the values of <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub> for all voltages. In this way, the contribution ratio for capacitive and ion diffusion can be calculated. For example, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>c is the fitted result at the speed of 0.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup> with the capacitive fraction shown in the blue region, while the capacitive contributions for all of the sweep rates are demonstrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>d. The capacitive contribution ratios are 63.5, 69.8, 72.6, 78.6, and 85.3% under sweep speed from 0.1 to 1.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. Similar kinetic properties have also been checked in SIB half-cells (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>).</div><div class="NLM_p">To reveal the ability of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids for practical application, LIB full cells were assembled, and their electrochemical properties have been investigated. The full cells were constructed with commercial LiFePO<sub>4</sub>(LFP) as the cathode and MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids as the anode (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>a, inset). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>a shows the charge/discharge profiles for the full cells between 0.60 and 3.60 V at 0.1C, revealing that the full cell delivered first charge/discharge capacities of 155/129 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> (calculated with the mass of LFP) with an initial Coulombic efficiency of 83%. Furthermore, in the cycling test (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>b), the full cell’s capacity retention after 125 cycles at 1C was 94.6%, which showed excellent stability. In addition, the full cells also presented superior rate performance, as determined in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>d. When the current density changed incrementally from 0.1C to as high as 10C, it delivered capacities of ∼129, 125, 112, 102, 90, 72, and 61 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. Afterward, the capacity could return to 100 and 121 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 1C and 0.2C, further revealing the high reversibility and stability of the full cells. The optical image in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>c shows that one single cell can light 37 red LED bulbs (operating voltage: 2 V), which further demonstrated its potential for practical energy storage application.</div><figure id="fig8" data-index="8" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 8</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/medium/am1c04776_0009.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0009.jpeg" id="gr8" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 8. Energy storage application of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G//LFP full cells: (a) charge/discharge profiles at 0.1C with an inserted schematic illustration of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G//LFP full cells, (b) cycling performance at 1C, (c) LED bulbs lighted by a single full cell, and (d) rate performance.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/asset/images/large/am1c04776_0009.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c04776&amp;id=fig8"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i19">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In conclusion, the monodisperse MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes in rock-salt structure have been fabricated using a facilely developed one-pot colloidal synthetic route from the reaction of Mn(II) acetylacetonate with dibenzyl dichalcogens in a mixed media of oleylamine with octadecene at 300 °C, and they presented with segregations and even point defects based on structure determinations using XRD, HRTEM, XPS, and BET techniques. They were successfully assembled to MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids by integrating the isolated MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes on the surface of N-doped graphene heterostructurally to form heterojunction-like hybrid composites, which were performed for the application of LIBs/SIBs for the first time. Disordered alloying of MnS and MnSe to the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes with defects is favorable for the generation of active sites increasingly. The introduction of N-doped graphene and the formation of heterointerface efficiently enhanced the electroconductivity and avoided the agglomeration of active nanocubes, which is favorable for the improvement of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids as anode for both lithium- and sodium-ion batteries with high performance. When functioned as anodes for Li/Na-ion batteries, the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids delivered a capacity of 1039/457 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> after 80/100 cycles, revealing excellent rate performance and long-term stability. Moreover, full-cell LIBs of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G//LFP have been constructed to light LED bulbs, which further demonstrated its promising practical application in the future.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i20">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c04776?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c04776</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Magnified XRD patterns of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes showing asymmetry (Figure S1); Raman spectra of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids (Figure S2); TEM and nitrogen adsorption–desorption isotherms (Figure S3); EDX spectra of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> nanocubes (Figure S4); lattice distortions in MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> (Figure S5); HRTEM images of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids (Figure S6); <i>ex</i><i>situ</i> XRD tests of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids for LIBs (Figure S7); electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) analysis of the bare MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub> electrode and the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrode for LIBs (Figure S8); TEM images of the MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrid electrode for LIBs and SIBs after 300 cycles (Figure S9); TGA curves for MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids with different N-G ratios and their cycling performance (Figure S10); kinetic analysis of MnS<sub>0.5</sub>Se<sub>0.5</sub>/N-G hybrids for SIBs (Figure S11); comparison of lithium storage performances (Table S1); and comparison of sodium storage performances (Table S2) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c04776/suppl_file/am1c04776_si_001.pdf">am1c04776_si_001.pdf (1.62 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c04776" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.  Although existing energy storage is dominated by pumped hydroelec., there is the recognition that battery systems can offer a no. of high-value opportunities, provided that lower costs can be obtained.  The battery systems reviewed here include sodium-sulfur batteries that are com. available for grid applications, redox-flow batteries that offer low cost, and lithium-ion batteries whose development for com. electronics and elec. vehicles is being applied to grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZwDymuubZm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj1xSYl4gbYdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsVGktL%252FJ&amp;md5=5035bfda7631ad9d075e8836e61146ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201104502"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reddy, A.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hybrid Nanostructures for Energy Storage Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Reddy, Arava Leela Mohana; Gowda, Sanketh R.; Shaijumon, Manikoth M.; Ajayan, Pulickel M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Materials engineering plays a key role in the field of energy storage.  In particular, engineering materials at the nanoscale offers unique properties resulting in high performance electrodes and electrolytes in various energy storage devices.  Consequently, considerable efforts have been made in recent years to fulfill the future requirements of electrochem. energy storage using these advanced materials.  Various multi-functional hybrid nanostructured materials are currently being studied to improve energy and power densities of next generation storage devices.  This review describes some of the recent progress in the synthesis of different types of hybrid nanostructures using template assisted and non-template based methods.  The potential applications and recent research efforts to utilize these hybrid nanostructures to enhance the electrochem. energy storage properties of Li-ion battery and supercapacitor are discussed.  This review also briefly outlines some of the recent progress and new approaches being explored in the techniques of fabrication of 3D battery structures using hybrid nanoarchitectures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpT8MtzGGIUjrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBdSsf0Bm_QA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xpt12rtL4%253D&amp;md5=560c789b8e16308a26828276a44905a1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201800561"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">30 Years of Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large Reversible Li Storage of Graphene Nanosheet Families for Use in Rechargeable Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yoo, EunJoo; Kim, Jedeok; Hosono, Eiji; Zhou, Hao-shen; Kudo, Tetsuichi; Honma, Itaru</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2277-2282</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The lithium storage properties of graphene nanosheet materials as high capacity anode materials for lithium secondary batteries were investigated.  Graphite is a practical anode material used for lithium secondary batteries, because of its capability for reversible lithium ion intercalation in the layered crystals, and the structural similarities of graphene nanosheet to graphite may provide another type of intercalation anode compd.  While the accommodation of lithium in these layered compds. is influenced by the layer spacing between the graphene nanosheets, control of the intergraphene sheet distance through interacting mols. such as carbon nanotubes or fullerenes (C60) might be crucial for enhancement of the storage capacity.  The sp. capacity of graphene nanosheet was found to be 540 mA-h/g, which is much larger than that of graphite, and this was increased up to 730 mA-h/g and 784 mA-h/g, resp., by the incorporation of macromols. of carbon nanotubes and C60 to the graphene nanosheet.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpszvzsL_AHOLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBdSsf0Bm_QA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXovFSks7s%253D&amp;md5=15db9a809d22a1ca95307ff78f307f3d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matsuda, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishii, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cumings, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Expanded Graphite as Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBdSsf0Bm_QA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2010.07.020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A review of the electrochemical performance of alloy anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wei-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Alloy anodes are promising anode materials for lithium-ion batteries due to their high-energy capacity and safety characteristics.  However, the com. use of alloy anodes has been hindered to date by their low cycle life and high initial capacity loss.  This overview highlights the recent progress in improving and understanding the electrochem. performance of various alloy anodes.  The approaches used for performance improvement are summarized, and the causes of first-cycle irreversible capacity loss are discussed.  The capacity retentions and irreversible capacity losses of various alloy anodes are compared.  Several alloy anodes exhibited excellent cycle life (up to 300 cycles) with high initial coulombic efficiency (80-90%) and large reversible capacity (500-700 mA-h/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrF3tp5C-HrMbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBdSsf0Bm_QA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhtFWntrnL&amp;md5=43d74909dbfa6369c172d63f845603df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201306314"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, B.     <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10297-10303</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">DTARAF</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanorod-FeP@C composites are synthesized via a one-pot soln. reaction of ferrocene (Fe(C5H5)2) with excess triphenylphosphine (PPh3) in sealed vacuum tubes at 390 °C, in which PPh3 is used as both the phosphorus source and solvent in the reaction.  The structure and lithium storage performance of the as-prepd. nanorod-FeP@C composites are intensively characterized, and it is interesting that the composites exhibit an increased capacity during cycling serving as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  Meanwhile, mechanism investigations reveal that the capacity increase of the composites results from a hysteretic lithiation of the nanostructured FeP phase due to the coating of the carbon shell in the composites.  Meanwhile, cyclic stability investigation shows that the composites have a very good cyclic stability that shows potential for the composites with a long lifespan as a promising kind of anode material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOpLcZrxn2r7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg0IOYp3Nl6og"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXntFWjtrY%253D&amp;md5=c88b2ac79ddaa5516d8b222420edb781</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700396"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ternary NiCoP nanoparticles assembled on graphene for high-performance lithium-ion batteries and supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Chunde; Qian, Yinyin; Yang, Jing; Xing, Shiqi; Ding, Xu; Yang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal phosphides have received considerable interest for electrochem. energy storage/conversion and catalysis.  In this work, we designed a unique hybrid of NiCoP nanoparticles adhered on quasi-planar structured graphene by assembling 8.5 nm ternary NiCoP nanoparticles on graphene through a soln.-phase self-assembly strategy.  The NiCoP catalyst in the form of small-size particles wrapped in graphene provided more active sites, a buffer for vol. alteration and enhanced cond. for electrochem. reactions.  Typically, the hybrid catalyst demonstrates a high specific capacity of around 532 mA h g-1, excellent cycling stability and superior rate performance when the hybrid material is evaluated as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, and it shows excellent electrochem. properties with a specific capacitance of 646 F g-1 at 4 A g-1, maintaining 91% of this initial value after 2000 cycles functioning as a supercapacitor.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq5Q2FLRCqeybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg0IOYp3Nl6og"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXnsl2qtLs%253D&amp;md5=2e531fc1d6ecb7bcbaf9f27c758d6b51</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.mattod.2019.11.008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Asif, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Transition Metal Chalcogenide Anodes for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Mater. Today</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>35</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">131</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">167</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.mattod.2019.11.008</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D35%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D131-167%26journal%3DMater.%2BToday%26author%3DZ.%2BAli%26author%3DT.%2BZhang%26author%3DM.%2BAsif%26author%3DL.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DY.%2BHou%26title%3DTransition%2BMetal%2BChalcogenide%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.mattod.2019.11.008&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c04776&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.mattod.2019.11.008&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Transition metal chalcogenide anodes for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ali, Zeeshan; Zhang, Teng; Asif, Muhammad; Zhao, Lina; Yu, Yan; Hou, Yanglong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">131-167</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1369-7021</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review Owing to the low cost and indefinite availability of sodium resources, rechargeable sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are now being considered as the most appealing alternatives to their lithium-ion counterparts for large scale applications.  On the other hand, transition metal chalcogenides (TMCs) have emerged as potential candidates of SIB anodes due to their versatile material species, ample abundance, low cost, robust nature and high theor. capacities.  However, TMCs still face several challenges like severe vol. changes during sodiation/desodiation, inadequate conductivities and large-scale productions.  Hence, many traditional and unconventional techniques have been developed to mitigate these issues and obtain high quality electrode materials for practical applications.  In this review, recent progress and the rectification stratagems of the problems of TMCs have been summarized firstly.  Then, a detailed comparison of transition metal selenides with sulfide TMCs family members was provided to investigate the factors which govern the relative performance improvements of selenides.  Besides this, multiple transition metals contg. TMCs (M-TMCs) have exhibited intriguingly better performances compared to mono-metal TMCs.  Hence, various inspirational features of M-TMCs were discussed.  As an outcome of these discussions, we were able to outline several outlooks and prospective solns. for the rectification of potential challenges of TMC anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoKkFsXSHZlqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhekuYmu2Trow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitlynurzF&amp;md5=6b0479032e86d7528e59860c6d1a59df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA02695E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuo, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered Tin Sulfide and Selenide Anode Materials for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered tin sulfide and selenide anode materials for Li- and Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei, Zengxi; Wang, Lei; Zhuo, Ming; Ni, Wei; Wang, Hongxia; Ma, Jianmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12185-12214</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered tin sulfides have attracted great interest as high-capacity anode materials in Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  In this review, we focus on the recent research progress in the area of design and synthesis of tin sulfide and selenide (SnS, SnS2, SnSe, and SnSe2) based anode materials for LIBs and NIBs.  After a brief introduction of the energy concerns and the development prospects of LIBs and NIBs, we further detailed the properties and advantages of tin sulfide and selenide based anode materials for LIBs and NIBs.  Besides the material structure design and optimization, the underlying mechanism and theor. anal. for improved electrochem. performance are also presented.  Addnl., comparison of tin sulfides and selenides is also provided.  Innovative strategies that have demonstrated the effectiveness of enhancing the performance of tin sulfide and selenide based anode materials for LIBs and NIBs are summarized.  We hope that this timely review can shed light on the research and development of tin sulfides and selenides as high-performance anode materials which are not only a good supplement to the material pool of commercialized LIBs, but also help facilitate the development of low-cost and sustainable NIBs for stationary energy storage in the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSCCpUDr8IzbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhekuYmu2Trow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVais77M&amp;md5=ffc2ad4c32b49ce55714efdffaec254d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.11.032"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Studies on Intrinsic Phase-Dependent Electrochemical Properties of MnS Nanocrystals as Anodes for Lithium–Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Studies on intrinsic phase-dependent electrochemical properties of MnS nanocrystals as anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hao, Yong; Chen, Chunhui; Yang, Xinyi; Xiao, Guanjun; Zou, Bo; Yang, Jianwen; Wang, Chunlei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">338</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9-16</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese sulfide (MnS), a member of transition metal sulfides, has been considered as a promising anode material for reversible Li storage due to its high theor. capacity and structural advantages.  However, the intrinsic electrochem. performance of MnS with different phases in lithium-ion batteries is yet to be fully investigated.  Herein, high purity rock-salt (RS), zinc-blende (ZB) and wurtzite (WZ) MnS nanocrystals with different morphologies were successfully synthesized via a facile solvothermal method.  The RS-MnS, ZB-MnS and WZ-MnS electrodes showed the capacities of 232.5 mAh g-1, 287.9 mAh g-1 and 79.8 mAh g-1 at the 600th cycle, resp.  ZB-MnS displayed the best performance in terms of specific capacity and cyclability in comparison to RS-MnS and WZ-MnS nanocrystals.  Interestingly, all the three kinds of MnS electrodes exhibited an unusual phenomenon of capacity increase upon cycling along with reduced particle sizes and without change in crystallinity.  The main contribution of capacity increase was ascribed to the decreased cell resistance and enhanced interfacial charge storage, which facilitated more effective Li+ diffusion into electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr5Y9muAx6JUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhekuYmu2Trow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvVChsbvK&amp;md5=9c67baaa8c60b1bd75435ff93126950b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/acs.inorgchem.5b02558"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of High-Quality α-MnSe Nanostructures with Superior Lithium Storage Properties</span>. <i>Inorg.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of High-Quality α-MnSe Nanostructures with Superior Lithium Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Na; Zhang, Yi; Zhao, Hongyang; Liu, Zhengqing; Zhang, Xinyu; Du, Yaping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2765-2770</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">INOCAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0020-1669</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-quality α-MnSe nanocubes were successfully prepd. for the first time by an effective hot injection synthesis strategy.  This approach was simple but robust and had been applied to the controllable synthesis of different sizes and diverse morphologies of α-MnSe nanostructures.  The crystal phases, compns., and microstructures of these nanostructures had been systematically characterized with a series of techniques.  As a proof-of-concept application, the as-prepd. α-MnSe nanocubes were used as an anode material for a lithium ion battery, which exhibited superior rate ability and ultralong cycle stability in half-cell and full-cell tests.  Importantly, the phase transition from α-MnSe to β-MnSe during the electrochem. process was proved by ex situ X-ray diffraction and selected area electron diffraction.  The excellent electrochem. performance of α-MnSe endowed its potential as an anode material candidate for high performance lithium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoR-k8W3VJ7ObVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhekuYmu2Trow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjvV2lsrw%253D&amp;md5=9419ce7d6691f6ecaac79584f6aa4a6b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b06590"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title"><i>In Situ</i> Synthesis of MnS Hollow Microspheres on Reduced Graphene Oxide Sheets as High-Capacity and Long-Life Anodes for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Synthesis of MnS Hollow Microspheres on Reduced Graphene Oxide Sheets as High-Capacity and Long-Life Anodes for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xijun; Ji, Shaomin; Gu, Mingzhe; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20957-20964</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Uniform MnS hollow microspheres in situ crystd. on reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanosheets via a facile hydrothermal method.  The MnS/RGO composite material was used as the anode for Na-ion batteries for the first time and exhibited excellent cycling performance, superior specific capacity, and great cycle stability and rate capability for both Li- and Na-ion batteries.  Compared with nonencapsulated pure MnS hollow microspheres, these MnS/RGO nanocomposites demonstrated excellent charge-discharge stability and long cycle life.  Li-ion storage testing revealed that these MnS/RGO nanocomposites deliver high discharge-charge capacities of 640 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 400 cycles and 830 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 100 cycles.  The MnS/RGO nanocomposites even retained a specific capacity of 308 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 after 125 cycles as the anode for Na-ion batteries.  The outstanding electrochem. performance of the MnS/RGO composite attributed to the RGO nanosheets greatly improved the electronic cond. and efficiently mitigated the stupendous vol. expansion during the progress of charge and discharge.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqgyxM_04H9CLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhekuYmu2Trow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVeqtrbI&amp;md5=76adb4195066af051b440c0c4f12fddd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA03967D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lü, H.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Coaxial α-MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Double Nanotubes as Superior Anode Materials in Li/Na-Ion Half/Full Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coaxial α-MnSe@N-doped carbon double nanotubes as superior anode materials in Li/Na-ion half/full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Dai-Huo; Li, Wen-Hao; Liang, Hao-Jie; Lu, Hong-Yan; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Wang, Jiawei; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">32</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15797-15806</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Coaxial nanotubes are a significant class of nanoscale building blocks for advanced electrodes of secondary batteries.  Herein, one-dimensional (1D) coaxial double nanotubes (DNTs) consisting of α-MnSe inner tubes and N-doped carbon (N-C) outer tubes (abbreviated as α-MnSe@N-C DNTs) are successfully prepd. and are demonstrated to be promising anode material for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries (LIBs/NIBs).  When used in LIBs, it was revealed by ex situ XRD/HRTEM studies and electrode kinetics that a new electrochem. α → β phase transition plays a crucial role in improving the cycling stability.  As a result, the α-MnSe@N-C DNTs electrode delivers a high Li-storage capacity (800 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1), excellent rate capability (405 mA h g-1 at 14 A g-1) and ultra-long cycling stability (a high capacity retention of 87.2% even after 9000 cycles at 2 A g-1) with retained 1D morphol.  In addn., the outer N-C nanotube can effectively protect the active α-MnSe inner nanotube to realize such outstanding electrochem. properties owing to the high elec. cond. and particular 1D coaxial nanoarchitecture of the inner nanotube.  Moreover, α-MnSe@N-C DNTs also exhibit excellent Li/Na-storage properties and full-cell performances when coupled with com. LiFePO4 and LiNi0.6Co0.2Mn0.2O2 cathodes in LIBs as well as with the Na3V2(PO4)2O2F cathode in NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4nAsrAP4oZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhIGm4fQof2ew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht12qtbzM&amp;md5=045ce6c324565054da697ba3f91ed983</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702383"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, D.     <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13952-13963</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybridizing carbonous matrix into metal sulfide is confirmed as an effective strategy to enhance electrode conductance and structure stability.  However, a comprehensive understanding of the interface reaction mechanism between active materials and carbon substrate is still urgently needed.  Based on the band energy theory, a route to enhance the rate ability for electrode is exploited on regulating interfaces of substrates/active heterojunction.  Herein, the highly stable Na+-storage performance of GeS2/3DG is delicately designed, where the hierarchical structure is enabled by uniformly overcoating GeS2 nanograins with graphene matrix.  Different from the widespread doping route of active materials for fast ion transfer, we focus on the effects of interface regulation on the high-rate Na- ion-storage performance of substrate/active materials.  Here, a well-designed interface of the C-Ge bond at the heterointerface induced by hierarchical GeS2/graphene heterojunction is pioneeringly explored, which can result in a fast electron transfer by reducing electron gathering polarization.  More importantly, defects in graphene can alleviate the polarization aroused by ion concn., which not only offers anchoring/doping sites for C-Ge bond but also provides extra ion channels for Na-ion transportation into GeS2.  This interface regulation of constructing metal-carbon bonds will shine light on the reaction kinetics and interface stability and contribute to the fundamental understanding of interface reaction mechanisms for metal sulfide anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqMn-ZF59V9ArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhIGm4fQof2ew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvVKhtLzL&amp;md5=93441f16527eaa0ef6380828bd38e49c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.snb.2020.129082"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Development of an Innovative Nitrite Sensing Platform Based on the Construction of Carbon-Layer-Coated In<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Porous Tubes</span>. <i>Sens.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Development of an innovative nitrite sensing platform based on the construction of carbon-layer-coated In2O3 porous tubes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dou, Baoting; Yan, Ji; Chen, Qian; Han, Xiguang; Feng, Qiumei; Miao, Xiangmin; Wang, Po</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sensors and Actuators, B: Chemical</span>
