                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-based dual-ion batteries via coupling high-capacity selenium/graphene anode with high-voltage graphite cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Xiankun; Li, Wenhao; Wang, Yingying; Li, Shaofang; Meng, Yunfeng; Yu, Haiyue; Chen, Baokuan; Wu, Xinglong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Chemical Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Dual ion batteries (DIBs) exhibit broad application prospects in the field of elec. energy storage (EES) devices with excellent properties, such as high voltage, high energy d., and low cost.  In the graphite-based DIBs, high voltage is needed to store enough anions with the formation of anion intercalation compd. XCn (X = AlCl-4, PF-6, TFSI-, etc.).  Hence, it is difficult for graphite-based DIBs to match proper anodes and electrolytes.  Here, an Se/graphene composite is prepd. via a convenient method, and assembled into a dual-ion full battery (DIFB) as anode with graphite cathode and 1 mol/L NaPF6 in EC:EMC (1:1, v:v).  This DIFB has achieved a high discharge capacity of 75.9 mA-h/g and high medium output voltage of 3.5 V at 0.1 A/g.  Actually, the suitable anode materials, such as the present Se/graphene composite, are extremely important for the development and application of graphite-based DIBs.  This study is enlightening for the design of future low-cost EES devices including graphite-based DIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqej6qI-51gbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhIGm4fQof2ew"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Strategies for improving the storage performance of silicon-based anodes in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tao, Wei; Wang, Ping; You, Ya; Park, Kyusung; Wang, Cao-Yu; Li, Yong-Ke; Cao, Fei-Fei; Xin, Sen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1739-1749</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon has attracted much attention as a promising anode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to its high theor. capacity and rich resource abundance.  However, the practical battery use of Si is challenged by its low cond. and drastic vol. variation during the Li uptake/release process.  Tremendous efforts have been made on shrinking the particle size of Si into nanoscale so that the vol. variation could be accommodated.  However, the bare nano-Si material would still pulverize upon (de)lithiation.  Moreover, it shows an excessive surface area to invite unlimited growth of solid electrolyte interface that hinders the transportation of charge carriers, and an increased interparticle resistance.  As a result, the Si nanoparticles gradually lose their elec. contact during the cycling process, which accounts for poor thermodn. stability and sluggish kinetics of the anode reaction vs. Li.  To address these problems and improve the Li storage performance of nano-Si anode, proper structural design should be applied on the Si anode.  In this perspective, we will briefly review some strategies for improving the electrochem. vs. Li of nano-Si materials and their derivs., and show opinions on the optimal design of nanostructured Si anode for advanced LIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">As a kind of novel multi-functional nanocomposite, a ternary hybrid of monodisperse Ni3S4 nanorods/graphitic C3N4 nanosheets/nitrogen-doped graphene with heterostructured architecture is controllably constructed for the first time, illustrating great potential for overall water splitting and the fabrication of sodium-ion batteries.  Intensive investigations revealed that the ternary hybrid with robust and intertwined nanostructures possesses shorter diffusion pathways, smaller diffusion resistance and faster transfer speeds of electrons and ions, which could expedite the transport of electrolyte to flood and interact with reaction sites, dynamically and thermodynamically.  Notably, the active Ni3S4 nanorods within the unique integrated ternary hybrid embedded in graphitic C3N4 nanosheets over a conducting substrate of nitrogen-doped graphene could strongly avoid agglomeration, abscission, anisotropic vol. expansion and irreversible mech. failure, even during extreme electrochem. reactions.  Owing to the integrated effect, the ternary hybrid delivers excellent electrochem. performance with long-term stability during water splitting and cycling durability when used in sodium-ion batteries.  In particular, a low onset potential of 40 mV (vs. RHE, J = -1.5 mA cm-2) is obsd. in the HER process, and the applied potentials are also as small as 1.47 V (vs. RHE) and 1.51 V for the OER and overall water splitting, resp., at 10 mA cm-2 under the same alk. conditions.  As for sodium-ion batteries, the ternary hybrid possesses an advanced specific capacity of ∼670 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 with particularly excellent rate capabilities and it could even work at a high c.d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtOLh8G8NMtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYf2q1v8MizQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXis1WhsLrN&amp;md5=1f8d615036c50f37e8a77ef22a4f4661</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1021/nl404165c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kravchyk, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Walter, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kovalenko, M.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Monodisperse Antimony Nanocrystals for High-Rate Li-ion and Na-ion Battery Anodes: Nano versus Bulk</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Meng; Kravchyk, Kostiantyn; Walter, Marc; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report colloidal synthesis of Sb nanocrystals with mean size tunable in the 10-20 nm range and with narrow size distributions of 7-11%.  In comparison to microcryst. Sb, 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals exhibit enhanced rate capability and higher cycling stability as anode materials in rechargeable Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  All three particle sizes of Sb have high and similar Li-ion and Na-ion charge storage capacities of 580-640 mA-h/g at moderate charging/discharging current densities of 0.5-1C (1C rate is 660 mA/g).  At all C-rates (0.5-20C, e.g. current densities of 0.33-13.2 A/g), capacities of 20 nm Sb particles are systematically better than for both 10 nm and bulk Sb.  At 20C rate, retention of charge storage capacities by 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals can reach 78-85% of the low-rate value, indicating that rate capability of Sb nanostructures can be comparable to the best Li-ion intercalation anodes and is so far unprecedented for Na-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5xNSHYkxGf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYf2q1v8MizQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs1Wmsbw%253D&amp;md5=6c9a0c090f52077a9b8eda7847cbfe2f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b13760"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Plasma-Induced Oxygen Vacancies in Urchin-Like Anatase Titania Coated by Carbon for Excellent Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Plasma-Induced Oxygen Vacancies in Urchin-Like Anatase Titania Coated by Carbon for Excellent Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gan, Qingmeng; He, Hanna; Zhao, Kuangmin; He, Zhen; Liu, Suqin; Yang, Shuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The incorporation of oxygen vacancies in anatase TiO2 has been studied as a promising way to accelerate the transport of electrons and Na+ ions, which is important for achieving excellent electrochem. properties for anatase TiO2.  However, wittingly introducing oxygen vacancies in anatase TiO2 for sodium-ion anodes by a facile and effective method is still a challenge.  In this work, we report an innovative method to introduce oxygen vacancies into the urchin-like N-doped carbon coated anatase TiO2 (NC-DTO) by a facile plasma treatment.  The superiorities of the oxygen vacancies combined with the conductive N-doped carbon coating enable the obtained NC-DTO of greatly improved sodium storage performance.  When served as the anode for sodium-ion batteries, the NC-DTO electrode shows superior electrochem. performance (capacity: 272 mA h g-1 at 0.25 C, capacity retention: 98.8% after 5000 cycles at 10 C, as well as ultrahigh capacity: 150 mA h g-1 at 15 C).  D. functional theory calcns. combined with exptl. results suggest that considerably improved sodium storage performance of NC-DTO is due to the enhanced electronic cond. from the N-doped carbon layer as well as narrowed band gap and lowered sodiation energy barrier from the introduction of oxygen vacancies.  This work highlights that introducing oxygen vacancies into TiO2 by plasma is a promising method to enhance the electrochem. property of TiO2, which also can be applied to different metal oxides for energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrtmRfuZXPUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYf2q1v8MizQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVars7g%253D&amp;md5=369a9fb337a78a3571adaffffe795d19</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2018.07.230"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vacancy-Induced Sodium-Ion Storage in N-Doped Carbon Nanofiber@MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheet Arrays</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vacancy-induced sodium-ion storage in N-doped carbon Nanofiber@MoS2 nanosheet arrays</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Jiaojiao; Wei, Zengxi; Wang, Caiyun; Ma, Jianmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a promising material for sodium-ion batteries, molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) affords excellent electrochem. performance owing to its large surface area and the accelerated electron transport within individual layers.  However, it suffers from slow reaction kinetics and agglomeration owing to low cond. and high surface energy.  In this work, nitrogen-doped carbon nanofiber@MoS2 nanosheets arrays with S-vacancies (NC@MoS2-VS) are developed via a process involving electrospining, hydrothermal and annealing.  When served as an anode material for SIBs, this material displays a superior capacity of 495 mAh g-1 over 100 charge/discharge cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, and the pseudocapacitive contribution is up to 74.4% as revealed by the cyclic voltammogram (CV) at 1 mV s-1.  The theor. calcns. show that the presence of sulfur vacancies facilitates the adsorption of Na+ and enhances the cond. of MoS2.  This work may pave a new avenue to develop other types of metal sulfides for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGratUmpFgtRubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYf2q1v8MizQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsVyntbjI&amp;md5=c7d10c509a8fecd99ee3403693b81698</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b05865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anion Vacancies Regulating Endows MoSSe with Fast and Stable Potassium Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Huang, Dan; Gan, Qingmeng; Hao, Junnan; Liu, Sailin; Wu, Zhibin; Pang, Wei Kong; Johannessen, Bernt; Tang, Yougen; Luo, Jing-Li; Wang, Haiyan; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Vacancy engineering is a promising approach for optimizing the energy storage performance of transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) due to the unique properties of vacancies in manipulating the electronic structure and active sites.  Nevertheless, achieving effective introduction of anion vacancies with adjustable vacancy concn. on a large scale is still a big challenge.  Herein, MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys with anion vacancies introduced in situ have been achieved by a simple alloying reaction, and the vacancy concn. has been optimized through adjusting the chem. compn.  Exptl. and d. functional theory calcn. results suggest that the anion vacancies in MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys could enhance the electronic cond., induce more active sites, and alleviate structural variation in the alloys during the potassium storage process.  When applied as potassium ion battery anodes, the most optimized vacancy-rich MoSSe alloy delivered high reversible capacities of 517.4 and 362.4 mAh g-1 at 100 and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  Moreover, a reversible capacity of 220.5 mAh g-1 could be maintained at 2000 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles.  This work demonstrates a practical approach to modifying the electronic and defect properties of TMDs, providing an effective strategy for constructing advanced electrode materials for battery systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXdcW5odM6NLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ligUgCigv-81Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVantrbK&amp;md5=bdf190a3483499180c6f2375a012a109</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201603219"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Novel Metal Chalcogenide SnSSe as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel Metal Chalcogenide SnSSe as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xusheng; Chen, Dong; Yang, Zhanhai; Zhang, Xiaohui; Wang, Chao; Chen, Jitao; Zhang, Xinxiang; Xue, Mianqi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel layered SnSSe material was introduced into a sodium ion battery as a high-performance anode with characteristid high capacity, superior cycleability, facile synthesis, and large-scale ease of prodn.  Within a voltage range of 0.1-3.0 V, the SnSSe electrodes delivered a high discharge capacity of 401 mA-h/g for the 900th cycle at 2500 and 330 mA-h/g after 1000 cycles at 5000 mA/g with no obvious capacity fading.  The unique characteristics of SnSSe, such as large interlayer spacing, preferred growth along the (001) crystal plane, and easily exfoliated lamellae, along with partial pseudocapacitive capacity contribution, may be the reasons for the excellent electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrkvLDhOv4tQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ligUgCigv-81Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtlChs7rJ&amp;md5=3810a0cc654c0575f0bb4f3eea564663</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.09.052"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Baker, A.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ternary tin selenium sulfide (SnSe0.5S0.5) nano alloy as the high-performance anode for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Qiming; Cui, Yanhui; Wu, Junwei; Qu, Deyang; Baker, Andrew P.; Ma, Yiheng; Song, Xiaona; Liu, Yanchen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">41</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">377-386</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal sulfides have received tremendous attention due to their superior electrochem. performance.  In this study, it is the first time that the ternary tin selenium sulfide, SnSe0.5S0.5, is investigated as a potential high-performance anode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The SnSe0.5S0.5/C nanocomposites have also been synthesized through a facile polyol-method followed by a simple hydrothermal process and subsequent sintering.  The material demonstrated a high specific capacity and a long-term cycling stability in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries (625 mA h g-1 for LIB at 500 mA g-1 rate after 1000 cycles, 430 mA h g-1 in a SIB at 200 mA g-1 rate after 100 cycles).  Furthermore, the kinetic anal. of Li-ions and Na-ions storage revealed that the extrinsic pseudocapacitive contribution could improve the charge transfer rate during the insertion and extn. of Li-ion and Na-ion, thus enhancing the rate performance and cycling stability.  These results demonstrated that the novel tin selenium sulfide (SnSe0.5S0.5) material could potentially be an excellent anode material for Li-ion storage and Na-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrge_eNtBA2W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ligUgCigv-81Q"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate cathode CrSSe based on anion reactions for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Si-Yu; Shi, Ding-Ren; Wang, Tian; Yue, Xin-Yang; Zheng, Lei; Zhang, Qing-Hua; Gu, Lin; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Shadike, Zulipiya; Li, Hong; Fu, Zheng-Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Studies of transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) can be traced back to the 1970s but they have been abandoned for a while due to the fire hazard of lithium metal batteries.  Herein, a new layered material, CrSSe, is reported, whose intercalative capacity can achieve 190 mA h g-1 with charges all compensated by anionic S and Se.  Fascinating performances of half-cells are also presented, with a capacity retention rate of 81.5% upon 1000 cycles at 20C and a high output of 101.7 mA h g-1 even at 200C.  In addn., an ideal way to build a type of full battery without lithium anodes for CrSSe is also displayed; a Li3N film was synthesized on the electrode surface as a lithium source.  Overall, the discovery of CrSSe enriches the chem. of TMDs and the application in full batteries opens up opportunities for enabling lithium-free cathodes to be widely utilized in practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpY9FLQrg0j_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ligUgCigv-81Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1Oit7nI&amp;md5=4db7c3213fe10771e119153c86b74673</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c16396"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, S.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of van der Waals Heterostructured FePSe3/Carbon Hybrid Nanosheets for Sodium Storage with High Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xing, Shiqi; Yang, Jing; Wang, Chunde; Zhou, Jianbin; Zhang, Jinhui; Zhang, Li; Yang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron phosphorus triselenide (FePSe3) is attractive for energy applications owing to its interesting layered geometry, electronic structure, and physiochem. property, while it is limited in actual application because of a very long fabrication time of over 7 days.  Herein, we report a new synthetic route to a high-quality sheetlike hybrid of iron phosphorus triselenide nanocrystals coated with graphitic carbon (FePSe3/C) as an alternative kind of van der Waals heterostructures for the first time via a pyrolytic process at 600°C from the precursors of ferrocene, red phosphorus, and selenium in a quartz tube with a significantly shortened reaction time of 24 h and even down to 30 min.  Investigations demonstrated that the component phase of FePSe3 in the layered FePSe3/C hybrid nanosheets is the rhombohedral phase, and the hybrid nanosheets other than bulk crystals are about 15 nm in thickness.  Acting as a cathode in fabricating half-cell sodium-ion batteries, the layered FePSe3/C hybrid nanosheets exhibited remarkable performance.  Typically, when c.d. was set as 50 mA g-1, the hybrid nanosheet-assembled battery exhibited a capacity of 182.7 mA h g-1 after performing over 50 cycles, and the nanosheet battery exhibited a capacity of 142 mA h g-1 after performing for 200 cycling trials at 1 A g-1 in the 0.8-2.2 V voltage window.  Meanwhile, the layered FePSe3/C hybrid nanosheets also exhibited very high rate capabilities at a relatively large c.d. in the present study, i.e., 172 and 95 mA h g-1 under typical performing conditions at 0.5 and 5 A g-1, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnZ9OyVKgkr7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ligUgCigv-81Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitlyisrvK&amp;md5=3ede03b3e937f7be1dd8c6f11dd6e712</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/ja01539a017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hummers, W.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Organometallic synthesis, structure determination, shape evolution, and formation mechanism of hexapod-like ternary PbSexS1-x nanostructures with tunable compositions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shao, Genrong; Chen, Guihuan; Zuo, Jian; Gong, Ming; Yang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Langmuir</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The fabrication of hexapod-like ternary PbSexS1-x nanostructures has been reported via an alternative organometallic route from reaction of Pb(II) salt with triphenylphosphine selenide (Ph3PSe) and dibenzyl disulfide (DBDS) in dibenzylamine (DBA) with addn. of oleic acid (OA) at 260 °C.  The shape, structure, and compn. of the nanostructured hexapods are investigated and detd. by techniques of XRD, SEM, TEM, Raman, HRTEM, SAED, XPS, EDX, and HAADF-STEM, and the obtained ternary nanostructured hexapods are of typical rock salt phase with Pb-rich features without phase sepn., and their compns. could be systematically regulated by facile variations of reaction parameters.  Investigations reveal that the successful fabrication of the ternary hexapods with tunable compns. is resulted from the effective selection of Se and S sources of Ph3PSe and DBDS that have similar reactivity in the current reaction system along with small lattice mismatch between the two end members of PbSe and PbS.  Generally, the relations between the compn. and lattice parameters for the ternary nanostructures obtained in DBA with varied addn. of OA exhibit linear slops that are consistent well with Vegard's law.  Interestingly, intensive investigations show that the nanostructures are mainly gradiently alloyed nanostructures with somewhat chalcogen-element segregations or disorders rather than homogeneously alloyed solid-state solns. due to kinetic limitation for short reaction time even though thermodn. is feasible in the system, and also, high concn. of S element in the feedstocks tends to relative high d. of disorders in the ternary nanostructures.  Based on the revealing of the formation mechanism for the nanostructures with varied microstructures, the ternary PbSexS1-x hexapods can be tuned from gradient alloys with segregations to approx. homogeneous via enlongating reaction time.  In addn., the photolysis of the nanostructures to lead oxysulfate and oxyselenate species is evidenced at ambient condition via Raman detection although they are stable at -190 °C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqS_uT8JJ69GbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhgmf_4XYJSyA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controlled growth of vertical 3D MoS2(1-x)Se2x nanosheets for an efficient and stable hydrogen evolution reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xiaoshuang; Wang, Zhiguo; Qiu, Yunfeng; Zhang, Jia; Liu, Guangbo; Zheng, Wei; Feng, Wei; Cao, Wenwu; Hu, PingAn; Hu, Wenping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) are considered as promising hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) candidates due to their exposed active sites at edges and superior electron mobility along sheets, however their inert basal planes and non-ohmic contact with current collectors greatly hamper their application in HER reactions.  Exposing active sites, accelerating charge transfer, and manipulating hydrogen adsorption free energy close to thermoneutral are significant to favor the HER process.  Herein, component-controllable 3D MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloy nanosheets with a vertically oriented architecture were successfully grown on conductive carbon cloth substrates through a CVD technique.  The bigger radius of Se can cause a slight distortion and bring about a polarized elec. field in the basal planes, resulting in favorable bond breaking of adsorbed mols.  Among all tested catalysts, Mo(S0.53Se0.47)2 alloy nanosheets exhibit the lowest Tafel slope (55.5 mV dec-1), smallest overpotential (183 mV) at 10 mA cm-2, and highest cond.  The Mo(S0.53Se0.47)2 alloy maintains its activity after 2000 cycles.  D. functional theory calcns. manifest adjustment of hydrogen adsorption free-energies and vacancy formation energies in MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloy nanosheets.  S and Se vacancies serve as a crucial factor for HER performance.  The 3D exposed active sites, adjusted hydrogen adsorption free energy, vacancy formation energies, and ohmic contact with carbon cloth are found to be responsible for the enhanced HER performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRkemZ0k5jZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhgmf_4XYJSyA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslCnsLjJ&amp;md5=62c21cf98223ed73bad0c509514acff8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.solener.2016.07.030"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Phase Segregation in CdTe/CdS Heterojunction and its Effect on Photo Current of CdTe Thin Films Solar Cell</span>. <i>Sol.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The phase segregation in CdTe/CdS heterojunction and its effect on photo current of CdTe thin films solar cell</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lv, Bin; Ma, Ligang; Li, Yun; Yan, Bo; Cai, Pinggen; Wu, Xiaoshan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solar Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The S-Te inter-diffusion in CdTe/CdS heterojunction has been studied by X-ray diffraction, Atomic force microscope and Spectroscopic ellipsometry.  For the first time, the phase segregation of CdTeySx compd. that is confirmed by X-ray measurement has been taken into account in the anal. of ellipsometry, which promotes the anal. reliability.  Benefit from the dielec. consts. obtained from the ellipsometric data, the external quantum efficiency of the solar cell has been fitted without any paradoxical assumption used before.  Results show that high temp. process such as Close space sublimation leads to significant S-Te inter-diffusion and shallows the junction obviously, but this does not happen in magnetron sputtered device.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-Dimensional Integrated MnS@Carbon Nanoreactors Hybrid: An Alternative Anode for Full-Cell Li-Ion and Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yani; Li, Linpo; Zhu, Jianhui; Meng, Ting; Ma, Lai; Zhang, Han; Xu, Maowen; Jiang, Jian; Li, Chang Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">27911-27919</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnS has triggered great interest as an anode material for rechargeable Li-ion/Na-ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs) because of its low cost, high electrochem. activity, and theor. capacity.  Nevertheless, the practical application is greatly hindered by its rapid capacity decay lead by inevitable active dissoln. and vol. expansions in charge/discharge cycles.  To resolve the above issues in LIBs/SIBs, the authors herein put forward the smart construction of MnS nanowires embedded in C nanoreactors (MnS@C NWs) via a facile soln. method followed by a scalable in situ sulfuration treatment.  This engineering protocol toward electrode architectures/configurations endows integrated MnS@C NWs anodes with large specific capacity (with a max. value of 847 mA h g-1 in LIBs and 720 mA h g-1 in SIBs), good operation stability, excellent rate capabilities, and prolonged cyclic life span.  To prove their potential application, the authors established the full cells (for LIBs, MnS@C//LiFePO4; for SIBs, MnS@C//Na3V2(PO4)3), both of which are capable of showing remarkable specific capacities, outstanding rate performance, and superb cyclic endurance.  This work offers a scalable, simple, and efficient evolution method to produce the integrated hybrid of MnS@C NWs, providing useful inspiration/guidelines for anodic applications of metal sulfides in next-generation power sources.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrqy_xMUzwrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhgmf_4XYJSyA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">P-type polycryst. Sn1-vS compds. and Sn0.985S1-xSex solid solns. are prepd. by combining mech. alloying (MA) and spark plasma sintering (SPS). Point defects provide high-frequency phonons scattering from the Se substitution in Sn0.985S1-xSex, in addn. to the strong scattering of mid-frequency phonons by dislocations.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cream roll-inspired advanced MnS/C composite for sodium-ion batteries: encapsulating MnS cream into hollow N,S-co-doped carbon rolls</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Gaojie; Chen, Kongyao; Wang, Yanjie; Wang, Zhuo; Chen, Xueli; Cui, Siwen; Wu, Zijie; Soutis, Constantinos; Chen, Weihua; Mi, Liwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">With advantages of high theor. capacity and low cost, manganese sulfide (MnS) has become a potential electrode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, complicated prepns. and limited cycle life still hinder its application.  Inspired by cream rolls in our daily life, a MnS/N,S-co-doped carbon tube (MnS/NSCT) composite with a 3D cross-linked tubular structure is prepd. via an ultra-simple and low-cost method in this work.  As the anode for SIBs, the cream roll-like MnS/NSCT composite has delivered the best electrochem. performance to date (the highest capacity of 550.6 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, the highest capacity of 447.0 mA h g-1 after 1400 cycles at 1000 mA g-1, and the best rate performance of 319.8 mA h g-1 at 10 000 mA g-1).  Besides, according to several in situ and ex situ techniques, the sodium storage mechanism of MnS/NSCTs is mainly from a conversion reaction, and the superior electrochem. performance of MnS/NSCTs is mainly attributed to the unique cream roll-like structure.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effective carbon constraint of MnS nanoparticles as high-performance anode of lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Paredes Camacho, Ramon A.; Wu, Ai-Min; Jin, Xiao-Zhe; Dong, Xu-Feng; Li, Xiao-Na; Huang, Hao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite possessing a high theor. capacity, MnS has a rather complex lithium kinetic diffusion and poor mech. stability that hinders its application in energy storage devices like lithium-ion batteries.  This study is focused on overcoming the drawbacks of MnS anode material by assembling a carbon-constraint MnS nanocomposite in a core-shell configuration.  This structure is obtained by a simple route involving DC plasma evapn. of Mn@C nanoparticles and posterior thermal sulfurization process.  As anode material in a Li-ion battery, MnS@C-300 attains high specific capacity of 890 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles at 500 mA g-1. This exceptional electrochem. response is endorsed to the synergetic effect of the smart design of a core-shell architecture.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanosized α-MnS homogenously embedded in axial multichannel carbon nanofibers as freestanding electrodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Xing-hai; Su, Kun-mei; Kang, Wei-min; Cheng, Bo-wen; Li, Zhen-huan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To buffer the unavoidable vol. expansion and structure collapse problems of transitional metal sulfides during lithiation process, herein, nanosized α-MnS homogenously embedded in axial multichannel C nanofibers was well designed and directly used as freestanding anodes for Li-ion batteries (LIBs).  The obtained C nanofibers were interwoven into a flexible and cross-linked film, which offered a 3-dimensional successive conductive networks and guaranteed sufficient contact interface for electrode/electrolyte.  The nanosized α-MnS was homogenously embedded into the C nanofiber framework and surrounded with a thin protective C layer, which effectively maintained the structural integrity for a satisfied cycling performance.  The high aspect ratio C nanofibers with axial open channels supplied sufficient active sites and formed long-range electronic pathways along the axial C wall.  Meanwhile, the radial voids provided enormous accommodation space to alleviate vol. expansion and shortened diffusion paths for faster ionic transfer.  Benefitting from the above unique merits, the freestanding electrodes delivered excellent Li storage performances and remarkable long-term cycling stability, including a high initial reversible capacity of 772 mA-h g-1 and excellent cycling capacity retention of 93.4% after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpXFtw7cXoZoLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifLZM6gW5Kew"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heteroatoms dual-doped hierarchical porous carbon-selenium composite for durable Li-Se and Na-Se batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Xiaosen; Yin, Lichang; Zhang, Tong; Zhang, Min; Fang, Zhibo; Wang, Chunzhong; Wei, Yingjin; Chen, Gang; Zhang, Dong; Sun, Zhenhua; Li, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">137-146</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Selenium (Se) is a prospective candidate of cathode material for high-energy batteries.  However, the dissoln. of high-order lithium selenides and the shuttle effect in electrolytes lead to low Se utilization, inferior capacity and poor cycling performance.  Herein, a heteroatoms (N and O) dual-doped hierarchical porous carbon (HDHPC) with interconnected macro/meso/micropores is used to confine Se composite and developed as a cathode material for advanced Li/Na-Se batteries in low-cost carbonate electrolyte.  For Li-Se batteries, Se/HDHPC cathode delivers an initial charge capacity of 613 mAh g-1 and maintains stable reversible capacity of 545 mAh g-1 with a capacity decay as low as 0.0074% per cycle after 1500 cycles at a c.d. of 0.5 C (1 C = 675 mA g-1).  For Na-Se batteries, Se/HDHPC exhibits a high initial charge capacity of 619 mAh g-1 and retains as high as 402 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles at a current rate of 0.5 C.  Moreover, Se/HDHPC composite also exhibits an excellent rate performance both in the Li-Se and Na-Se batteries even at a high rate up to 20 C (13.5 A g-1).  Such excellent electrochem. properties of Se/HDHPC are mainly contributed from two aspects.  One is the hierarchical porous structure of the HDHPC, which benefit the penetration of electrolyte and also act as micro reaction chambers to effectively suppress the vol. change of the electrode.  The other is the strong interaction between lithium/sodium selenide and carbon host induced by heteroatoms (N and O) dual-doping, which can strongly anchor the Se-contained species, thus preventing the side reaction of Se anions with electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqUM8s-6xuDCbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifLZM6gW5Kew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXotlCrsLg%253D&amp;md5=c9e8940c4e1a9fa6a8dd9306bbaec7eb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1038/nature12385"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geim, A.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Van der Waals heterostructures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Geim, A. K.; Grigorieva, I. V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">499</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7459</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">419-425</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Research on graphene and other two-dimensional at. crystals is intense and is likely to remain one of the leading topics in condensed matter physics and materials science for many years.  Looking beyond this field, isolated at. planes can also be reassembled into designer heterostructures made layer by layer in a precisely chosen sequence.  The first, already remarkably complex, such heterostructures (often referred to as van der Waals') have recently been fabricated and investigated, revealing unusual properties and new phenomena.  Here we review this emerging research area and identify possible future directions.  With steady improvement in fabrication techniques and using graphene's springboard, van der Waals heterostructures should develop into a large field of their own.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpA35hIzMsc5bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifLZM6gW5Kew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFKnu7rN&amp;md5=58b3fc8bf8d8e656719bfaa23ab0e99b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b03349"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Functional Three-Dimensional Graphene/Polymer Composites</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">7231</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7247</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Functional Three-Dimensional Graphene/Polymer Composites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Meng; Duan, Xidong; Xu, Yuxi; Duan, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Integration of graphene with polymers to construct three-dimensional porous graphene/polymer composites (3DGPCs) has attracted considerable attention in the past few years for both fundamental studies and diverse technol. applications.  With the broad diversity in mol. structures of graphene and polymers via rich chem. routes, a no. of 3DGPCs have been developed with unique structural, elec., and mech. properties, chem. tenability, and attractive functions, which greatly expands the research horizon of graphene-based composites.  In particular, the properties and functions of the 3DGPCs can be readily tuned by precisely controlling the hierarchical porosity in the 3D graphene architecture as well as the intricate synergistic interactions between graphene and polymers.  In this paper, we review the recent progress in 3DGPCs, including their synthetic strategies and potential applications in environmental protection, energy storage, sensors, and conducting composites.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering graphene and TMDs based van der Waals heterostructures for photovoltaic and photoelectrochemical solar energy conversion</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Changli; Cao, Qi; Wang, Faze; Xiao, Yequan; Li, Yanbo; Delaunay, Jean-Jacques; Zhu, Hongwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene and two-dimensional (2D) transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) have attracted significant interest due to their unique properties that cannot be obtained in their bulk counterparts.  These atomically thin 2D materials have demonstrated strong light-matter interactions, tunable optical bandgap structures and unique structural and elec. properties, rendering possible the high conversion efficiency of solar energy with a minimal amt. of active absorber material.  The isolated 2D monolayer can be stacked into arbitrary van der Waals (vdWs) heterostructures without the need to consider lattice matching.  Several combinations of 2D/3D and 2D/2D materials have been assembled to create vdWs heterojunctions for photovoltaic (PV) and photoelectrochem. (PEC) energy conversion.  However, the complex, less-constrained, and more environmentally vulnerable interface in a vdWs heterojunction is different from that of a conventional, epitaxially grown heterojunction, engendering new challenges for surface and interface engineering.  In this review, the physics of band alignment, the chem. of surface modification and the behavior of photoexcited charge transfer at the interface during PV and PEC processes will be discussed.  We will present a survey of the recent progress and challenges of 2D/3D and 2D/2D vdWs heterojunctions, with emphasis on their applicability to PV and PEC devices.  Finally, we will discuss emerging issues yet to be explored for 2D materials to achieve high solar energy conversion efficiency and possible strategies to improve their performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7UnFGSr8QnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lheNdCU8_AflQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulating MnSe Nanoparticles Inside 3D Hierarchical Carbon Frameworks with Lithium Storage Boosted by in Situ Electrochemical Phase Transformation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Tao; Liu, Jianwen; Zhang, Manshu; Yang, Dexin; Zheng, Jianhui; Ju, Zhijin; Cheng, Jianlin; Zhuang, Jinyang; Liu, Yangai; Zhong, Jiasong; Liu, Hao; Wang, Guoxiu; Zheng, Rongkun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrode materials that act through the electrochem. conversion mechanism, such as metal selenides, have been considered as promising anode candidates for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), although their fast capacity attenuation and inadequate elec. cond. are impeding their practical application.  In this work, these issues are addressed through the efficient fabrication of MnSe nanoparticles inside porous carbon hierarchical architectures for evaluation as anode materials for LIBs.  D. functional theory simulations indicate that there is a completely irreversible phase transformation during the initial cycle, and the high structural reversibility of β-MnSe provides a low energy barrier for the diffusion of lithium ions.  Electron localization function calcns. demonstrate that the phase transformation leads to high charge transfer kinetics and a favorable lithium ion diffusion coeff.  Benefitting from the phase transformation and unique structural engineering, the MnSe/C chestnut-like structures with boosted cond. deliver enhanced lithium storage performance (885 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1 after 200 cycles), superior cycling stability (a capacity of 880 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles), and outstanding rate performance (416 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGouaT0G5osEALVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lheNdCU8_AflQ"> &gt;&gt; Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3581</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3589</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Scalable Strategy To Develop Advanced Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Commercial Fe3O4-Derived Fe3O4@FeS with Superior Full-Cell Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Bao-Hua; Wang, Ying-Ying; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Zhang, Yu; Ning, Qiu-Li; Yang, Yang; Li, Wen-Hao; Zhang, Jing-Ping; Wang, Xin-Long; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3581-3589</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel core-shell Fe3O4@FeS composed of Fe3O4 core and FeS shell with the morphol. of regular octahedra has been prepd. via a facile and scalable strategy via employing com. Fe3O4 as the precursor.  When used as anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the prepd. Fe3O4@FeS combines the merits of FeS and Fe3O4 with high Na-storage capacity and superior cycling stability, resp.  The optimized Fe3O4@FeS electrode shows ultralong cycle life and outstanding rate capability.  For instance, it remains a capacity retention of 90.8% with a reversible capacity of 169 mAh g-1 after 750 cycles at 0.2 A g-1 and 151 mAh g-1 at a high c.d. of 2 A g-1, which is about 7.5 times in comparison to the Na-storage capacity of com. Fe3O4.  More importantly, the prepd. Fe3O4@FeS also exhibits excellent full-cell performance.  The assembled Fe3O4@FeS//Na3V2(PO4)2O2F sodium-ion full battery gives a reversible capacity of 157 mAh g-1 after 50 cycles at 0.5 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 92.3% and the Coulombic efficiency of around 100%, demonstrating its applicability for sodium-ion full batteries as a promising anode.  Furthermore, it is also disclosed that such superior electrochem. properties can be attributed to the pseudocapacitive behavior of FeS shell as demonstrated by the kinetics studies as well as the core-shell structure.  In view of the large-scale availability of com. precursor and ease of prepn., this study provide a scalable strategy to develop advanced anode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBb7Gs4YJuHrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZcFU65A0pYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXksVOltg%253D%253D&amp;md5=800f289306f9a89a1b2e0f9cecf93dea</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref60'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b11984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Double-Morphology CoS<sub>2</sub> Anchored on N-Doped Multichannel Carbon Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">31441</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">31451</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.8b11984</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D31441-31451%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DY.%2BPan%26author%3DX.%2BCheng%26author%3DL.%2BGong%26author%3DL.%2BShi%26author%3DT.%2BZhou%26author%3DY.%2BDeng%26author%3DH.%2BZhang%26title%3DDouble-Morphology%2BCoS2%2BAnchored%2Bon%2BN-Doped%2BMultichannel%2BCarbon%2BNanofibers%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.8b11984&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c04776&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11984&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Double-Morphology CoS2 Anchored on N-Doped Multichannel Carbon Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yuelei; Cheng, Xudong; Gong, Lunlun; Shi, Long; Zhou, Ting; Deng, Yurui; Zhang, Heping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">31441-31451</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (NIBs) have attracted increasing attention given the fact that sodium is relatively more plentiful and affordable than lithium for sustainable and large-scale energy storage systems.  However, the shortage of electrode materials with outstanding comprehensive properties has limited the practical implementations of NIBs.  Among all the discovered anode materials, transition-metal sulfide has been proven as one of the most competitive and promising ones due to its excellent redox reversibility and relatively high theor. capacity.  In this study, double-morphol. N-doped CoS2/multichannel carbon nanofibers composites (CoS2/MCNFs) are precisely designed, which overcome common issues such as the poor cycling life and inferior rate performance of CoS2 electrodes.  The conductive 3D interconnected multichannel nanostructure of CoS2/MCNFs provides efficient buffer zones for the release of mech. stresses from Na+ ions intercalation/deintercalation.  The synergy of the diverse structural features enables a robust frame and a rapid electrochem. reaction in CoS2/MCNFs anode, resulting in an impressive long-term cycling life of 900 cycles with a capacity of 620 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 (86.4% theor. capacity) and a surprisingly high-power output.  The proposed design in this study provides a rational and novel thought for fabricating electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIewUzTT2U7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZcFU65A0pYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhs1WitLnF&amp;md5=d5a670e5d0bfd28f24c4512e95fa9d03</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref61'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.8b02861"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Inverse Capacity Growth and Pocket Effect in SnS<sub>2</sub> Semifilled Carbon Nanotube Anode</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">8037</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">8047</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.8b02861</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D8037-8047%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DX.%2BJin%26author%3DH.%2BHuang%26author%3DA.%2BWu%26author%3DS.%2BGao%26author%3DM.%2BLei%26author%3DJ.%2BZhao%26author%3DX.%2BGao%26author%3DG.%2BCao%26title%3DInverse%2BCapacity%2BGrowth%2Band%2BPocket%2BEffect%2Bin%2BSnS2%2BSemifilled%2BCarbon%2BNanotube%2BAnode%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.8b02861&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c04776&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b02861&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Inverse Capacity Growth and Pocket Effect in SnS2 Semifilled Carbon Nanotube Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Xiaozhe; Huang, Hao; Wu, Aimin; Gao, Song; Lei, Mingkai; Zhao, Jijun; Gao, Xiaoxia; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8037-8047</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnS2 with high theor. capacity has been impeded from practical applications as the anode of lithium-ion (Li-ion) batteries due to its large vol. expansion and fast capacity decay.  A nanostructure of the SnS2 semifilled carbon nanotube (SnS2@CNT) has been realized by plasma-assisted fabrication of Sn semifilled CNT (Sn@CNT) followed by post-sulfurization.  When serving as the anode of a Li-ion battery, SnS2@CNT delivers an initial discharge capacity of 1258 mAh g-1 at 0.3 A g-1.  Instead of capacity fading, SnS2@CNT shows inverse capacity growth to 2733 mAh g-1 after 470 cycles.  The high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy images show that the void in CNTs, after cycling, is fully filled with pulverized SnS2 grains which have a shortened Li-ion diffusion path and enhanced surface area for interfacial redox reactions.  In addn., the CNTs, like a pocket, confine the pulverized SnS2, maintain the elec. contact and structural integrity, and thus allow the electrodes to work safely under long cyclic loadings and extreme temp. conditions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmBpg3tmUMxLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZcFU65A0pYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsVWit7rN&amp;md5=37311a3c2050663a7be97ba12605e4de</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref62'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit62" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA03552G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A rGO–CNT Aerogel Covalently Bonded with a Nitrogen-Rich Polymer as a Polysulfide Adsorptive Cathode for High Sulfur Loading Lithium Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of high capacity Li-S batteries is hampered by both the shuttle effect of polysulfides and low sulfur areal loading problems.  To inhibit the shuttle effect, a polysulfide adsorptive polymer polyethylenimine (PEI) is covalently bonded with reduced graphene oxide (rGO) in a 1-step hydrothermal reaction.  Multi-walled C nanotubes (MWCNTs) are simultaneously interweaved with rGO.  The resultant PEI-rGO-MWCNT aerogel (PEI-GC) provides ample chemisorption domains of amine groups and abundant elec. contact sites.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. prove a binding energy of 2.43 eV between PEI and polysulfide.  The PEI-GC cell achieved a high capacity of 933 mAh/g for the 500th cycle at 1C, stable rate performance up to 10C, and low self-discharge rate.  The covalent bond between PEI and rGO experiences no degrdn. during the 500 cycles.  PEI-GC achieved excellent cycling performance at a high S loading of ≤18 mg/cm2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2l_um2qlT6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZcFU65A0pYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXpvVKjt7s%253D&amp;md5=5ed5ac524738486ae5c422e15e385f24</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref63'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit63" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA05297B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Dispersed Zn Nanoparticles Confined in a Nanoporous Carbon Network: Promising Anode Materials for Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly dispersed Zn nanoparticles confined in a nanoporous carbon network: promising anode materials for sodium and potassium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Chunliu; Gu, Xin; Zhang, Li; Wang, Ying; Yan, Liting; Liu, Dandan; Li, Liangjun; Dai, Pengcheng; Zhao, Xuebo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Highly dispersed Zn nanoparticles confined in a nanoporous carbon network (ZNP/C) are prepd. by directly annealing a Zn-contg. metal-org. framework in an inert atm. and investigated as an anode material for sodium and potassium ion batteries for the first time.  ZNP/C has unique structural features, such as highly dispersed Zn nanoparticles, a nanoporous carbon network and a high surface area, which can efficiently enhance the reactivity, facilitate ion/electron transportation and buffer vol. changes, and thus greatly improve its Na/K storage performance.  As a sodium ion battery anode, ZNP/C-600 shows a high capacity of 361 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, and an ultrahigh capacity of 227 mA h g-1 is sustained after 1000 cycles at 2 A g-1.  When employed as a potassium ion battery anode, ZNP/C-600 exhibits a high capacity of 200 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, and a stable capacity of 145 mA h g-1 over 300 cycles at 0.5 A g-1.  Qual. and quant. analyses reveal that capacitance and diffusion mechanisms account for the superior Na/K storage performance, in which the capacitance plays a significant role.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGowWpWzdujtObVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZcFU65A0pYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsVWjs7zO&amp;md5=0dca22871c52887b29e55d517af3dab3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref64'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.1021/nn100740x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.                         cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin MoS2 Nanosheets Supported on N-doped Carbon Nanoboxes with Enhanced Lithium Storage and Electrocatalytic Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Xin-Yao; Hu, Han; Wang, Yawen; Chen, Hongyu; Lou, Xiong Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
